Paris – The Ministry of War announced today, "All border guards have been ordered to be on alert," which shows the tense atmosphere in Europe after Germany re-stationed troops in the Rhineland region. However, the Ministry of War denied that it would mobilize immediately, but said that there were currently 32,000 armed soldiers, and 500,000 more could be mobilized at any time, not including reservists. If the existing troops must be increased, it is not necessary to mobilize, but only to summon the border guard reserves and give them appropriate training. (National Telegraph, 11th) sanctions against Italy, saying that this matter was not mentioned at all. Although the number of war hawks in the House of Representatives is still small, it is increasing at any time. The Communist Party and the radical leftists mostly advocate war, but although the Socialist Party hates Hitler, it does not advocate the use of force. There are also some moderates who believe that Germany's current financial and economic situation is extremely dangerous. If strict economic sanctions can be imposed, their effectiveness should not be less than that of military sanctions. The government, in view of the divergence of opinions in the House of Representatives, is now considering adjourning it in the middle of next week to cover it up. (National Telegraph, 11th)

British Hold Special Cabinet Meeting; League of Nations Meeting May Be Postponed 37

London – The cabinet met at 11 a.m. this morning at the Prime Minister's residence at 10 Downing Street. The public did not pay attention. There is a possibility of postponing the League of Nations Council meeting scheduled to be held in London on Saturday. The decision depends on the progress made by the conference of representatives of the signatory countries to the Locarno Pact held here this afternoon. (Reuters, 12th)

London – Regarding the conference of signatory countries to the Locarno Pact, the cabinet held a special meeting at 11 a.m. today to discuss the situation in Paris. Foreign Secretary Eden and Lord Privy Seal Halifax answered the questions raised by the cabinet members one by one. It is reported that Eden and Halifax expressed the opinion that if Britain's attitude in the current crisis is weak, the European situation will inevitably have a serious impact, and said that France is already prepared to sever diplomatic relations with Germany and demand that economic and financial sanctions be imposed on Germany. (Havas, 12th)

London – The British cabinet met at 11 a.m. this morning at 10 Downing Street to discuss the crisis caused by Germany's treaty abrogation. The meeting lasted for an hour, but no major decisions were made, as it wanted to wait for the results of the talks between British and French diplomats at the French Embassy this afternoon. The British cabinet has not set a date for the next meeting, but all cabinet members are prepared to meet at any time. (Reuters, 12th)

London – Foreign Secretary Eden and Lord Privy Seal Halifax arrived here from Paris this morning. The cabinet immediately convened a meeting at 5:30 p.m. to hear reports from Eden and Halifax on the conference of signatory countries to the Locarno Pact in Paris. According to the Foreign Office, after hearing the report, the cabinet was quite shocked by the attitude adopted by France, and at the same time, it became more aware of the critical state of the situation. The Foreign Office believes that at this moment, Führer Hitler should be made aware of the need to rein in the horse before the precipice, so as to ease the current situation, and then a way can be found to start negotiations. Although there is currently no concrete proposal on this matter, most people advocate that Germany should withdraw some of its troops stationed in the Rhineland Province and promise not to set up fortifications along the Rhine River. If Germany is unwilling to make concessions automatically, then Britain, France, Belgium, and Italy may jointly uphold the Locarno Pact regardless of Germany's treaty abrogation and exert spiritual pressure on Germany, or even take a further step and have the countries concerned conclude a military agreement, which is also possible. It is reported that the cabinet was quite concerned that the Soviet Union, the Little Entente, and the Balkan Entente countries all expressed support for the stance adopted by France. However, British public opinion advocates adopting a compromise and opposes imposing pressure or sanctions on Germany, which is enough to hinder the cabinet's actions. (Havas, 11th)

Belgian Prime Minister's Statement: Prepared to Participate in Collective Action, but also Willing to Negotiate a New Treaty 41

Brussels: Prime Minister Janson, in his speech to the Chamber of Representatives today, used fervent language regarding Germany's abandonment of the Locarno Pact, urging everyone to remain calm, use common sense, and make rational decisions to protect children from the horrors faced by modern people. He stated that Germany's excuse was the Franco-Soviet Mutual Assistance Pact, which has nothing to do with Belgium. There is no political agreement or military obligation between France and Belgium. People have always believed that international organizations should not be based on violence but should be founded on agreements. This belief has now been shattered by Germany's actions, and it may take generations to recover, which is truly regrettable. He feels that if the signatories of the Locarno Pact can unite and take collective action, then we can escape danger; otherwise, the world may face dire consequences. Belgium is ready to participate in any collective action, agreeing to cooperate with France and Britain. At the same time, Belgium will uphold the Locarno Pact until a new one replaces it. (Reuter's dispatch, 11th)

Brussels: Janson continued, stating that Belgium's border with neighboring countries is longest with Germany, and the area is a plain with no natural defenses. Therefore, Germany's re-establishment of defenses in the Rhineland area seriously endangers Belgium's security. As for Germany's abandonment of the Locarno Pact, it is also groundless as far as Belgium is concerned, because Belgium was not a signatory to the Franco-Soviet Mutual Assistance Pact. Janson then read out the recent military agreement between the French and Belgian general staffs, stating that Belgium's security depends on this agreement. Back in 1920, France and Belgium originally had a military agreement that applied to the situation arising from the Allied occupation of the Rhineland after the European War. Now, times have changed, and the old agreement is no longer practical. Therefore, the French and Belgian general staffs have revised a new one to replace the old one. Its purpose is to maintain close contact between the two general staffs so that they can fulfill the obligations stipulated in the mutual assistance clauses of the Locarno Pact when necessary. This agreement was approved by France on March 6, just one day before Germany abandoned the Locarno Pact. Janson also commented on the proposals in the German memorandum, saying that some suggestions seem to be constructive and of interest to Belgium. However, Belgium's security is threatened by Germany's re-establishment of defenses in the Rhineland area. Therefore, if any agreement is concluded based on Germany's proposals, it should be supplemented with appropriate compensation to ensure that Belgium's security is not diminished. (Havas dispatch, 11th)

The Netherlands Begins Alert: Soldiers Whose Service Term Expired Will Not Be Discharged 42

Educational Broadcasting Special Issue

A Brief Discussion on Soil Improvement Methods (Part 1) 71

— Zhang Naifeng, Technician at the Central Agricultural Experiment Station

Ladies and gentlemen: Today's educational broadcast is my turn to talk about a brief discussion on soil improvement methods. The soil I am going to talk about is the soil used in agriculture, which is what plants rely on to grow. Originally, soil has many uses, such as building roads, building houses, making bricks and tiles, making pottery, and so on. However, most of the soil is used for planting. The main crops all grow on the soil, so the soil I am going to talk about is the soil used for planting.

Before talking about improvement, we should first know what good soil is like and what bad soil is like, and then we can talk about how to turn bad soil into good soil. This is the order of my topic. In other words, what I am going to talk about is, first, the conditions of good soil, second, the types of bad soil, and third, how to improve the soil.

The influence of soil on the plants growing on it can be divided into the following six factors: first, providing moisture; second, providing air; third, providing warmth; fourth, providing nutrients; fifth, being free from diseases and pests; and sixth, having sufficient depth to allow the roots of plants to fully develop. These six are the factors provided by the soil that can control plant growth. If one of them is deficient, the plants above cannot grow to a perfect extent.

Plants need a lot of water. Generally speaking, every pound of dry plant, whether it is rice straw or grains, needs 300 to 600 pounds of water to nourish it. Air is equally important. If the air is not ventilated, the plant will suffocate. Moreover, there is a lot of carbon gas in the soil. If it is not regulated, the plant will also be injured. As for temperature, most of it depends on the weather, and a small part also depends on the soil. Some soils are warm, and some soils are relatively cold. If it is too cold, the plant cannot grow, or even freeze. If it is too hot, the plant will also die from the heat. As for the nutrients of the plant, of course, it depends on the soil supply, and the soil should not contain any disease or pest components, so as not to hinder the growth of the plant. Finally, the soil must also have sufficient depth, generally about two or three feet deep. If it is less than two or three feet, only a few plants can grow, and large plants will not work.

If the soil is good, then its texture must be neither loose nor sticky. The soil particles are about two or three centimeters in diameter. If, in the same place, one type of soil has a large block structure and the other has a small granular structure, then the soil with the large block structure must be worse. Listeners, don't think that all soils are the same as what you see. If you pay attention when you have the opportunity, you can see many different structures, different colors, and different properties. If you take it to the chemical laboratory for chemical testing, then there will be more different properties. Furthermore, if good soil is dug down, the top seven or eight inches should be very loose, and the bottom should be slightly harder, but not so hard as to be like a brick. When digging seven or eight feet deep, there should be water underneath. The above describes the physical properties of good soil. As for its chemical properties, it should be rich in nutrients and organic matter (that is, humus), and should be neither alkaline nor too acidic, generally between PHS. 5.0-7.0. Also, the soluble salt content in the soil should be below 0.1 percent. If the physical properties are good and the chemical properties are also good, then the microbial properties must also be appropriate. This kind of good soil directly regulates the six factors mentioned earlier. These six factors are moisture, air, temperature, nutrition, and the opportunity for plant roots to develop to the bottom.

The types of bad soil can be divided into six types: climate-related, terrain-related, soil sodification-related, and improper use-related.

Climate has a great influence on soil. The reason why a soil becomes a certain type of soil is because of the climate. Regarding this point, I will not prepare to talk about it in detail today, but only talk about two situations in which the soil is bad because of the climate. The first is too dry. When it is too dry, it is because of lack of water. As I said before, growing one pound of dry plant needs 300 to 600 pounds of water. Therefore, lack of water can directly affect the physiological functions of the plant. Because in this case, not only the nutrients in the soil are not easy to dissolve, but also the opportunity for plants to absorb nutrients is reduced. Soil that lacks water often lacks humus. Even if there is plant matter buried in the ground, it is not easy to rot because there is too little water. Moreover, such soil often does not have a leaching effect, and soluble salts such as calcium carbonate and calcium sulfate remain in the soil, creating a soil rich in soluble salts. The existence of a large amount of salt in the soil is harmful to plants. The second is too wet. If there is too much water, the air in the soil will be reduced, and the plant will suffer from lack of air. Also, because there is too much water, many oxidation processes in the soil stop. At the same time, the evaporation of water requires a lot of heat, so wet soil is also colder. All of the above situations are not conducive to plant growth.

Terrain has a great influence on soil. The soil on the small slopes is often washed away by rainwater. Not only the nutrients and humus in the soil are washed away by rainwater, but even the entire topsoil is washed away to the bottom. The subsoil (that is, the so-called raw soil) exposed due to the loss of topsoil is often very barren. The newly opened soil mountain is very good for the first two years, but after planting for a few years, it will not work. This is mostly because of this reason. The soil at the bottom of the slope is good because it receives nutrients and humus washed down from the slope. However, there are also unnecessary salts washed down, which makes the land at the bottom of the slope worse. Secondly, in terms of water distribution, the water in the soil on the hillside is easy to lose, while the water in the valley at the bottom of the hillside is not easy to drain. These are all the harms of bad terrain.

The relationship between the texture of the soil and the properties of the soil can be divided into two types: one is too loose and the other is too sticky. Too loose soil is sandy soil. Its problem is the lack of clay, therefore, it does not have the ability to retain water. When rainwater comes down, it is immediately drained away. It also does not have the ability to retain nutrients. After applying fertilizer, it is soon lost. Moreover, when there is a big wind, there is a danger of the entire sandy soil being blown away by the wind. Too sticky soil is not easy to cultivate, and because of its stickiness, not only air cannot circulate, but also water cannot be regulated. When there is a lot of rainfall, there is too much water, and when there is little rainfall, there is not enough water. Secondly, because there are many fine particles in the sticky soil, it swells when wet and shrinks when dry, so the soil is easy to crack. In this case, plant roots are easily injured. Indeed, clay soil often has a great ability to absorb water in many cases, but although there is a lot of water in the soil, plants cannot use it. At the same time, it also has a great ability to absorb fertilizer, but after applying fertilizer, it is often not easy to see results. In short, too sticky soil, because of the various influences of physical, chemical, and microbial aspects, causes it to undergo an unsanitary change, which is not suitable for general crops.

When the soil layers are not suitable, it can also make the soil very bad. Some soils have a hard layer of bedrock underneath. This layer is very hard, making it impossible for plant roots to penetrate, and rainwater from the sky also cannot penetrate. Some soils have a layer of loose sand underneath. In dry weather, water cannot rise up. Another type is that the soil is very thin, and there are stones below a few inches. These three types are all unsuitable soil layers.

So-called soil sodification refers to the fact that after a soil is eroded by salt, it initially has a lot of salt, and slowly the sodium in these salts erodes the texture of the soil. That is to say, these salts not only exist in the soil but also have a chemical effect with the soil. Such soil is often too sticky when wet and often very hard when dry, and the soil clumps are very large, the soil fertility is very low, and the plants that are planted are prone to problems if the rainfall is slightly unsuitable.

The above five types of bad soil can be summarized as naturally bad soil. The sixth type is man-made bad soil. Man-made bad soil is because the nutrients in the soil have been continuously used without adequate replenishment, so it becomes worse and worse. This situation is very common in our China. The reason: one is because there is not enough fertilizer, and the other is because there is no attention paid to a good crop rotation system, so this result occurs. However, this kind of man-made bad soil is easy to improve. Just apply the appropriate fertilizer. As for how to apply the appropriate fertilizer, this issue is very complicated, and I will not prepare to talk about it in detail today.

Communications from Western Regions

Travel Notes of Qinghai (Continued) 73

— Zhuang Xueben

Geography and History: Regarding our two-day investigation in Tangba Fort, the locals have a general understanding.

Tangba Fort is divided into six villages: 1. Tangba Fort, 2. Baiya Village, 3. Yaitou Village, 4. Xiaosi Village, 5. Caizi Gully, 6. Tangba Village. All are located on the east bank of the Shatang River and are now divided into two townships, Jinhua and Gonghe. Previously, there were only thirteen households, namely Tangba Major Household, Changshou Major Household, Yaitou Household, Yong'an Household, Xinzhuang Household, Xiaosi Household, Bulong Household, Xiaozhuang Household, Erlangbao Household, Tieling Household, Gongta Household, Dacaizi Household, and Yaomu Household. However, it has now grown to four hundred households; eighty percent are purely local people, and twenty percent are Han people who have migrated here.

During the late Qing Dynasty, they still had a Tusi system, under the jurisdiction of the Dongqi Tusi. Under the Tusi, there was also a Qianzong, a Bazong, and two Zongguans.

The ancestors of the Dongqi Tusi: Duo Liangzhi Shijieshi, were Chuantou people from the Western Regions, and served as the Right Minister of the Gansu Province during the Yuan Dynasty. In the fourth year of Hongwu in the Ming Dynasty, he was awarded the hereditary post of Commander Qian Shi. His son Duan Zhu succeeded to the post in the twenty-ninth year of Hongwu and died in battle, posthumously awarded the title of General of the Flying Cavalry and赐姓祁. By the tenth generation grandson, Qi Bingzhong, in the nineteenth year of Wanli, he inherited the position of Commander Tongzhi. Later, for his meritorious service, he was promoted to Chief Supervisor of the Ji Liao Left Capital Commander, added the title of Junior Guardian of the Crown Prince, and erected a monument in the middle of Jiehuang. By the Qing Dynasty, Qi Guoping, the son of Bingzhong, submitted in the second year of Shunzhi and inherited the post of Commander Tongzhi in the ninth year. He had two sons, Qi Bozhizhong, both of whom had martial talents. Bozhi was promoted to Luan Yi Shi for his merits, and Zhongzhi became a Jinshi in the ninth year of Kangxi and later promoted to Deputy General of Jinhua, Zhejiang for his merits. Later generations inherited the title. Now they live in Shengfangou, four miles north of Ledu County. Qi Huan is his descendant. (The above is recorded in "The Recent Qinghai")

Therefore, their Daolas sing about the history of their Tusi General Qi. After the establishment of the Republic of China, several sober-minded locals submitted a complaint to the Xining Prefecture, and from then on, the title of Qi Tusi was abolished. Tangba Fort was also freed from the Tusi's control. Before August of the nineteenth year, when the new Huzhu County was not yet established, this place was under the jurisdiction of Xizhai County.

Women are Diligent, Men are Lazy

The locals of Tangba have long abandoned the nomadic society and live by farming mountain land. However, their habits are still similar to those of nomadic societies. Family and field work are centered on women. Lazy men, except for cultivating the land, do not care about anything else in the fields or at home. Crops are harvested once a year because the local climate is very cold, with long winters and short summers. Hailstorms are also common in summer, and it snows in August and September. Therefore, crops are planted at the beginning of summer and harvested at the beginning of autumn. The main crops are Qingke barley, wheat, and soybeans.

Few of them are engaged in commerce. Handicrafts are also immature, only able to make felt and Hezi (wool cloth). Therefore, their economy is not very prosperous. Those with five or six mu of land, one or two cows, and a dozen sheep are called "Xiaoda Households," – a small well-off family. Lending interest rates are very high, generally from 2.5% to 4.5%. Land prices are very low, only worth 50-60 Chuan per mu, which is about 10 yuan in national currency. Taxes are very high, and each mu of land must pay 50-60 Chuan in grain tax per year. There are also many other corvée duties. Wages are very low. The price for doing hard labor for others every day, in addition to providing meals, is only 5 to 10 cents.

Unique Costumes

The clothing of the locals: children over four or five years old mostly do not wear trousers. Now, in the winter when it is ten degrees below zero, their calves are frozen like red radishes. Wealthy men wear cloth clothes like Han people, and ordinary people use Hezi to make clothes. The style is the same as the Han people's long gowns. They also have yellow skin, dark brown eyeballs, and black hair, and flat faces. After wearing Han clothes, they cannot be distinguished from Han people. However, the decorations of their women are worth introducing. During ordinary work periods! Cloth trousers, long Hezi clothes, waistbands, barefoot, wearing brimmed felt hats. In summer, they wear small round bamboo hats in the style of umbrellas. During New Year's festivals, they wear red-sleeved clothes, tie floral belts, wear silver rings hanging down like chains in both ears, and wear a large necklace around their necks: the necklace is full of white clam shells polished like copper coins. Hair ornaments: Wearing a red hat that rises more than a foot high, like a dustpan. The hat is made of red cardboard and wire, and the edges are all drooping red tassels. Because it looks like a dustpan, it is commonly called a "Dustpan Head." Behind it, a silver bowl-style ornament with embroidery covers their hair bun, and another silver or copper hairpin a foot long is inserted horizontally behind their heads. The red tassels on their foreheads are triangular, like old-fashioned bangs. Adult women, the unmarried, have a wide red border on the trouser legs, and the married have a black border. This can also be considered some external distinction between virgins and married women.

Sleeping with Cattle and Sheep

Their diet is mainly Qingke barley and wheat; made into noodles, or 　, or fried into Ba. In summer, wild vegetables are added to the noodles, called "Green Grass Rice." Usually, men like to drink alcohol, which is brewed from Qufu grain and yeast and can be drunk in ten days. The color is clear and the taste is light. Because it is easy to drink, they get drunk every time they drink.

Most of the houses are square bungalows, with a circle of earth walls outside, forming a courtyard. Chickens, dogs, and pigs are raised in the middle, and it also serves as a pen for cattle and sheep. The houses are mostly divided into three or four rooms with earthen walls. The middle room is used as a scripture hall for hanging god statues and for entertaining guests. One side is the bedroom. One side is the kitchen. The younger generation and calves and lambs in winter sleep in the kitchen. The sleeping earthen pit is connected to the stove. A short earthen wall separates them. Cooking is done in front, and people sleep behind. They don't need to burn the pit separately in the cold winter nights, which is a smart and economical method for them. They sleep in a very mixed way. Most men and women sleep together. Like the Fan people, they don't have quilts. When they sleep, they untie their belts, and the clothes they wear during the day become their bedding at night.

Marriage and Funeral Customs

The customs of the locals: the social interaction between men and women is very open. Boys and girls of the same age make friends, called "Holding Hands." Men make friends with men, called "Sworn Brothers." Women make friends with women, called "Sworn Sisters."

However, their marriages are mostly decided by their parents. There is a matchmaker who comes and goes to mediate, and they cannot get rid of the habit of autocracy. The betrothal gifts include cattle, sheep, livestock, cloth, felt, Qingke barley, wine, etc., depending on the economic situation of the man's family. The rich pay 70-80 yuan, and the poor pay 20-30 yuan. They use livestock as transportation to pick up the bride. Upon entering the door, they worship heaven and earth, and the bride enters the kitchen. At this time, the woman's relatives also come to the man's house for a banquet. Everyone sits around in the garden in front of the village; they hold wine jars decorated with a piece of wool and begin to "Daola," singing and drinking, praising each other, taking pride in those who have many songs and crisp voices. The wine banquets the man's family uses to treat relatives include fried , vegetable buns, etc., divided into three courses: The first course is called "Panshan Tea," the second course is called "Shaomai Tea," and the third course is called "Beef Rib Tea."

Now, marriage is also relatively free, but after the two parties are aligned, they must still go through the process of parental matchmaking. The age of marriage is mostly under fifteen years old.

Funerals mostly use cremation. After a local dies, the corpse is carried to the wilderness, and a Lama is invited to chant scriptures to transcend the soul. An earthen pit is dug, and a fire is built to cremate the corpse.

Religious Beliefs

The religion of the locals is also Lamaism, so families with several sons must send one or two to become Lamas. Every densely populated village must have a village temple. On the tops of the high mountains near the village, a pile of Mahayana trees is piled up, a few branches are inserted, and a few sutra cloths are hung, serving as their mountain god.

They have a deep belief in the guardian deity arrow. The guardians have names such as "Five Platform Guardian," "Cow Head Guardian," and "Sheep Head Guardian." They all have a guardian enshrined in their homes. They also have considerable faith in Lamason "Mule Heavenly King"; the Mule Heavenly King is a blue-faced, fanged, ugly deity riding a green mule. He does not have a very high position in Lamaism. In addition, they also pay considerable respect to the Garuda bird and the twelve gods.

On the slopes near the village and at the intersections of the main roads, many "Pengkang" are built. A Pengkang is a square object with mud Buddhas "Zhacha" sealed in the middle, printed with wooden boards. Such Pengkang are originally also found near Lama temples in various places, but the locals build more because they have great faith that Pengkang can block the hail disasters in summer. Before the Pengkang were built in the local villages, there were many hail disasters, but they gradually decreased afterward. On the first and fifteenth of each month, and during their spare time, they mostly circle around it, chanting Om Mani Padme Hum, praying.

Locals do not wash their faces very much, let alone take baths. Because they do not pay attention to hygiene, they suffer from many diseases. When they get sick, they go to the temple to make a wish or invite a god. They are superstitious about divine power. Once, we were wandering around in the village. A local held a sick child and wanted us to raise our feet and step on his little head, so that the child could recover from illness and prolong life. We could only follow his instructions and step on it.

Coal Mines by the Roadside

On the evening of the third day, we returned to the county government and spent the night. On January 27th, early in the morning, the county magistrate sent Director Wang and a policeman, along with several livestock, to take us to Hongkangzigou, sixty miles east of the county; because we needed to conduct further investigations in more purely local villages.

We left the east gate at ten o'clock, facing the sun. Five miles to Donggou, which is also a local village. Several red-clothed local women visiting relatives were holding children and riding white horses, reflecting the white snow on the mountain peaks and the solid ice in the gully, forming a beautiful and harmonious picture.

Below, there were few traces of people. Ten miles through Halazhigou, which is also a huge river in Huzhu. Gray-black coal was found along the gully. Although the quality on the surface is very poor, there must be better coal seams underneath.

After climbing over two relatively high earthen mountains, the horses' hooves stepped onto the edge of Hongya Zigou. Peaceful locals looked at several new travelers with surprise. After passing through a slender poplar forest, a row of earthen houses on the hillside to the left came into view. The policeman led my livestock to stop in front of an earthen wall. Several locals greeted us respectfully and carefully took our blankets and spread them on the fire pit in the main room, inviting us in.

Here, there are wide courtyards, spacious houses, and neat mangers. In the past, it was the Yamen of Tusi Sang Siege Li. At dusk, an emaciated and aging old man of sixty-five, supported by illness, came out to greet us. He was Tusi Li Chengxiang. We were entertained by him and stayed here for five consecutive days, until after the "You Ning Temple" Devil Dance on the eighth day, before returning to Xining.

Shandong Province Motor Road Starts Carrying Mail 74

Mail Transportation Agreement Has Been Finalized

Civilian Communication is Increasingly Convenient

Jinan Communication: The construction industry in this province is making rapid progress. The provincial telephone network has been completed early. In addition to the government transmitting orders, it is also open to the public. Civilian transmission is convenient, but the cost is still too high, so we must pay attention to mail delivery. Naturally, mail delivery is rapid along the Jinpu and Jiaoji railways. Those farther away from the railway are still extremely inconvenient. Taking the counties in Jiaodong, Luxi, and Lunan as examples, letters sent to Jinan often take three or four days. Jinan newspapers sent to various counties still lack interest because the news is delayed, which has a major impact on culture. In recent years, the motor roads in this province have been expanded one after another, reaching more than 10,000 miles. Although they carry passengers, they do not transport mail. Letters and packages are still mostly transported by porters or old-fashioned carts, so they cannot be fast. The people suffer from this. Recently, the Shandong Provincial Postal Administration and the Provincial Motor Road Administration have finalized a contract for transporting mail. The Motor Road Administration reported to the Construction Department, and Construction Director Zhang Honglie presented it to the provincial government's political affairs meeting for discussion today (the 11th). It was resolved to approve it, and the post office and the Motor Road Administration will determine the date and start transportation immediately. This is truly a new era in the transportation of this province. The contract signed by the Post Office and the Motor Road consists of 25 articles, and the transportation method is stipulated in great detail. The routes are divided into two types: one is the transportation route, and the other is the agency for escorting and transporting routes. The types of transportation include letters, postcards, ordinary registered newspapers, printed matter, trade contracts, samples, etc., small packages within the weight limit, and occasional packages, as well as all official business to and from the post office, can also be transported. Each route opens once a day each way, and the specified weight is limited to 500 kg for the Yanwei Road, and 150 kg for other roads (if the Yanwei Road Bureau operates official cargo vehicles, it may transport large packages, and the package limit and remuneration will be determined separately by both parties at that time). All mail transported by the post office, light mail, is exempt from freight. For heavy mail, the remuneration is one cent per kilogram for every 100 Chinese miles. In order to save the trouble of classification and calculation, 20% of the total weight is used as free light mail, and the remaining 80% is used as the weight of heavy mail for which remuneration should be paid. It will be settled and paid at the end of each month. Regarding the agent transportation, the post office sends an escort to escort the vehicle along the way. If there is any damage, the Motor Road Bureau is not responsible. The escort can ride the car for free. If the Motor Road Bureau acts as an agent for escorting and transportation, the Motor Road Bureau is responsible. The post office pays the Motor Road Bureau a considerable subsidy for the escort every month.

First Constructed by Mantetsu, Still Managed by Mantetsu

The Japanese Will Use It to Counter Russia and Mongolia and Control North China

Jinzhou Communication: The Jin Cheng Railway, commissioned by the puppet organization to Mantetsu to construct and manage, was announced by Mantetsu on the 1st of this month to start business on March 10th. It is verified that the completion of the line is the 436-kilometer railway between Jinzhou and Chengde, which is now fully open. This line crosses Rehe and occupies an extremely important position militarily. On the one hand, it can deal with Soviet Russia and Mongolia, and on the other hand, it can control Hebei, Chahar, and other provinces. The Japanese have planned carefully and thoroughly, and on the surface, it is said to be for business purposes, to facilitate travel and transportation of industries. According to its scheduled timetable, from March 10th, Train 3 will depart from Jinzhou at 7:00 a.m. and arrive in Chengde at 9:50 p.m. Train 4 will depart from Chengde at 7:00 a.m. and arrive in Jinzhou at 9:50 p.m. In the future, it will run according to this timetable. The Japanese also boasted that the projects in Pingquan and Chengde were the most difficult, because the number of tunnels and bridges is said to be unique among all "Manchukuo" railways. Most of them are along the river, so the scenery is excellent, and there are historical sites in Chengde, which can be called the only tourist railway in Northeast China. (Northeast News Agency)

Honor of Zou Yixin, a Female Astronomer Studying in Japan 76

Currently Diligently Studying at the Azabu Observatory

Japanese Newspapers Praise Her as the Shining Star of Astronomy

Tokyo Communication: Zou Yixin, a Chinese astronomer, was originally an assistant professor at the Guangzhou National Sun Yat-sen University Observatory. Last spring, she was sent to Japan by Zou Lu, the president of the university. After arriving in Japan, she studied diligently and was praised by scholars in Japan. Although the Tokyo Imperial University, which never accepts female students, also specially approved her admission to study. Newspapers here have reported on this matter. The Tokyo Asahi Shimbun on January 8th of this year praised Ms. Zou as the only female astronomer in the Orient and a brave woman. Recently, a reporter from the "Miyako Shimbun" personally visited the Azabu Observatory to see Ms. Zou and asked for permission to take pictures. After returning, he wrote an article in the Miyako Shimbun on February 17th. The article praised her as the shining star of the observatory and praised her extremely. It is truly a highlight for the Chinese students studying in Japan. Now, the original text is translated as follows: "Ms. Zou, who is slender and dressed in a celadon Chinese dress, is truly a unique highlight in the ancient and majestic Azabu Observatory built by the Ministry of the Navy, which has a Meiji flavor. She is a top student at Sun Yat-sen University. After graduating, she immediately served as a technician at the astronomical observatory of her alma mater and wrote papers such as "Research on Sunspots." With such a young age and such achievements, her future is indeed infinitely promising. After the cherry blossoms bloomed last spring, she came to Japan to study. She first entered the Taiho School to learn Japanese, and then entered the observatory. Her daily conversations with the director and professors are naturally in Japanese, but when it comes to academic conversations, she uses English entirely. She also takes notes, attends lectures, and observes with telescopes. She is extremely enthusiastic about research and is truly a shining star of the observatory. She also reports to her alma mater every month. After returning to China, she will become a professor at her alma mater. It is also heard that Ms. Zou was married last year, and her husband is also an astronomer. He will be sent to France by Sun Yat-sen University next month. Because of the mission of Chinese academics, these two young people have to temporarily part ways like loving swallows. It is heard that the astronomical terms used in their correspondence are more than the words of love of newlyweds," etc. According to the observatory staff, since the construction of the observatory, there have been two Chinese students, both men. They returned to China seven or eight years ago and are now university professors. Ms. Zou is the only female student studying astronomy, and she is thought to be the only one in the Orient. From the director to the professors, they all praise Ms. Zou extremely. I look forward to O'Ddy Yun.

Chaoshan: Strictly Prevent Smuggling 77

—Newly Revised Regulations for Unpacking, Transporting, and Selling Rice and Beans—

Shantou Correspondence: Last year, smuggling was rampant in the Chaoshan area. The smugglers had powerful backgrounds and illegally imported large quantities of rice and beans. They established numerous branch offices in the market towns of Chaozhou and Meizhou counties. These smuggled goods were first escorted by ruffians into the interior, and then the smugglers found ways to sell them off. Even today, smuggled goods continue to flow into Shantou unabated. Some unscrupulous merchants collude with foreign smugglers, committing all sorts of evils. When smuggled goods are seized by anti-smuggling checkpoints and tax police, ruffians come forward to demand their return. As a result, tax evasion incidents occur frequently. Furthermore, the anti-smuggling tax police conduct searches and inspections with extreme strictness, which sometimes leads to the mistaken seizure of goods on which taxes have already been paid. Last month, the Chaoan Chamber of Commerce, based on a petition from the Rice and Bean Industry Association, stated that Chaoan City is a distribution center for goods from the upper and lower reaches of the Han River. Sometimes, the tax-paid certificates affixed to the bags are lost en route. If the original bags of rice and beans must be opened for retail sale, Shantou also needs to repackage the original bulk into smaller containers before selling. Without opening and unpacking, it is impossible to sell; opening and unpacking risks being suspected by the tax police of repackaging or dealing in smuggled goods, and many merchants have been arrested and fined. The merchants feel it is unacceptable to be mistakenly charged with criminal offenses, and they have specially petitioned the Agricultural Tax Bureau to request the Finance Department to find a remedy to alleviate the merchants' difficulties. Yesterday, Xiao Sheng, the director of anti-smuggling in Shantou, resigned, and the Finance Department appointed Ye Hanzhi, the anti-smuggling commissioner for the Southern Route, to succeed him in Shantou. He also issued a "Regulation for Unpacking, Transporting, and Selling Rice and Beans," which was forwarded to the Shantou North and South Port Grain and Miscellaneous Goods Association for compliance as follows: All unpacking, transporting, and selling of foreign rice and beans must be declared to the local tax collection office or anti-smuggling agency before unpacking, so that personnel can be dispatched to supervise the unpacking. Foreign beans and other legumes that are sold in loose form must have the sales receipts submitted to the tax collection office or anti-smuggling agency for inspection, stamping, and release. The agency will register the quantity on the sales receipt for auditing purposes. When carrying goods accompanied by inspected sales receipts, the anti-smuggling checkpoints along the way should verify that the goods match the items on the receipt and release them immediately. If the retail quantity is within 50 catties and there is a formal merchant's sales receipt, reporting and inspection may be waived. Merchants who sell foreign rice and beans in loose form must report the retail quantity to the local tax collection office or anti-smuggling agency for verification on a ten-day basis. The report form must be submitted on the day following the end of each day. If domestically produced bean oil from places where the Agricultural Tax Bureau or tax collection office is established is transported and sold, a guarantee must be filled out in accordance with the Finance Department's order, together with the oil mill's sales receipt, and submitted to the Agricultural Tax Bureau or tax collection sub-office for guarantee and verification. A transportation permit will be issued to accompany the goods. For domestically produced oil sold in places where there is no tax bureau office, the "Regulations for the Free Transportation and Sale of Domestically Produced Oil" sent by the Provincial Assembly shall be followed. All sales receipts from domestically produced oil mills, as well as customs release forms and certificates from the local township office or chamber of commerce, should be inspected and released. The above regulations can be said to be extremely strict, but merchants feel that the procedures are very troublesome.

Suzhou

The Ministry of Finance, in order to investigate the stamp tax in Wuxian County, specially dispatched Li Guoqi, together with Tong Yixiang, a member of the Suzhou Finance Department, to Suzhou. Wujiang Secretary Accepts Bribes and Will Be Sent to the Provincial Capital

Huang Heng, who resides at No. 2 Taohuawu in Liumen, accepted bribes and committed malfeasance while serving as the secretary of the Wujiang County Anti-Smoking Association last year. After the Jiangsu Supervisory Envoy's Office dispatched personnel to investigate, Huang was arrested and sent to the Wujiang County Government for detention by the security team. It has been proven by the bribing soil vendors such as Cai Zhiqian that Huang received a bribe of 1,800 yuan, delivered in two installments at the Lao Danfeng Restaurant and Lu Wang Ruiyu Teahouse in Suzhou. County Magistrate Xu was greatly angered and has submitted a request for instructions to the province. It is rumored that he will be sent to the Zhenjiang Provincial Security Office for investigation.

Wind and Rain Devastate Incense Snow Sea

Dengwei Mountain in Guangfu Township, Suzhou, is planted with plum trees within ten li, and is known as the Incense Snow Sea. Every year during the first and second months of the lunar calendar, tourists flock there. This year, the spring cold was particularly severe, and there was continuous rain and snow. Until today, the plum blossoms of Dengwei have not yet bloomed, so there are few tourists. Although a few people still go to explore the plum blossoms, they all return disappointed. According to the locals, the plum blossoms have been devastated by the wind and rain this year, and their roots have been damaged. Even if they bloom when the weather warms up, they may not be as prosperous as in previous years, and the fruit production will be greatly affected in the future.

Wuxi

筹建公共大會堂

筹建公共大會堂

This district's first district office held its 75th district affairs meeting yesterday, resolving the following: The office's expenditure report for October to December of the 24th year has been compiled and reported to the county for record and should be retroactively acknowledged. The staff members of the township offices in this district should undergo short-term training, with the district office formulating implementation measures. In a democratic nation, people's gatherings are of utmost importance, but this district lacks a suitable venue. It is proposed to construct a public assembly hall, with the district head serving as the preparation director and the township heads serving as the preparation members, named the "First District Public Assembly Hall," with a provisional budget of 10,000 yuan. The entire district has only seven small vegetable markets. Temporary vegetable markets should be set up in prosperous street areas. Self-government research associations keep self-governance information that can be claimed from the township offices. Obey the order to bury floating coffins on the Jinghu and other roads to prioritize public health. Obey the universal vaccination methods order; township offices should publicize the benefits of vaccination and find ways to implement them. The replacement of roadside trees on Tonghui Road within the district this year will have its location determined by the district office and planned for implementation.

Flour Mills All Shut Down

There are four flour mills in this county: Maoxin Numbers 1 and 2, Jiufeng, Tailong, etc. Their flour has a wide sales area, reaching various provinces in North China. Since the September 18th Incident, the loss of the Northeast has greatly impacted sales. In recent years, due to droughts and floods in various regions, sales have seen a rebound and become profitable. Last summer, the wheat harvest in various regions was poor, and the mills could not procure raw materials smoothly. Furthermore, the price of wheat has been increasing daily, almost as expensive as rice. Since the start of operations this year, the flour market has been even better, and the mills have been processing goods around the clock. However, raw materials are scarce, and the rice shops have also sold out their stocks. The mills have sent personnel to various counties to purchase, but the counties also have no grains to spare. Therefore, they have been forced to shut down in the past two days. Currently, the mills have less than 40,000 bags of flour in stock, and the flour shops have only slightly more than 10,000 bags in stock. If there is no import of foreign wheat or flour, prices will inevitably rise. Yesterday (12th), the market price of flour shops was 3.42 yuan per bag for Green Mountain Foot and Green Battleship brands, and 3.27 yuan per bag for Red Mountain Foot. The noodle shops will also raise prices soon.

Jiangyin

Communications Soldier Commits Suicide Out of Patriotism

Song Xueyun, a communications soldier of the 552nd Regiment of the 87th Division of this county, around 30 years old, from Hunan, suddenly committed suicide with a rifle at 7:30 PM the day before yesterday. The bullet entered through the stomach and exited through the back, piercing the stomach. He immediately fell to the ground, groaning in a pool of blood. After being discovered, he was immediately sent to the Shensu Yiyuan Hospital in Dongchu for treatment. It is said that the reason for Song's suicide was that he felt that the foreign troubles were becoming increasingly urgent, the national affairs were deteriorating, and there was no joy in life, so he committed suicide.

Jiangsu Provincial Chamber of Commerce Holds Extraordinary Joint Meeting

The Jiangsu Provincial Chamber of Commerce held a joint meeting of executive and supervisory members in March yesterday, chaired by Yu Xiaochuan. Matters for discussion: The Wuxian Chamber of Commerce proposed to continue forwarding the case for the addition of auxiliary coins. It was resolved that the association would continue to petition for the addition and also write to the chambers of commerce in other provinces and cities to jointly advocate for it. The Yixing Chamber of Commerce proposed that inland copper coins are flooded. Is it feasible to petition the provincial government to order all counties to comply with the standards of the Ministry's order and not freely expand or contract in order to provide relief? Resolution: Telegraph the Ministry of Finance to notify the three banks of China, Communications, and Bank of China to comply with the ministry's standard of 300 copper coins and 12 silver dimes per silver dollar, and, depending on the circumstances of each region, redeem as much as possible to stabilize market prices and provide a standard rate. The Yixing Chamber of Commerce proposed that the dime notes issued by various banks have the same face value but different styles, making them difficult to distinguish. It is proposed to petition the Ministry of Finance to order the banks to clearly distinguish the grades of the face value of the new dime notes issued in the future by size and color for easy identification. Is it feasible? Resolution: Forward the case as is. The Changshu Chamber of Commerce proposed that the business tax on soybean cakes and wheat gluten be increased by order. At this time of rural decline and commercial depression, please continue to collect it at 2 per mille to reduce the burden on the people. Resolution: Forward the case as is to the Ministry of Finance. The Yule District Chamber of Commerce cited a letter from the Pharmaceutical Industry Association stating that the members of the association total just over a dozen. Those who are capable of handling affairs serve as executive and supervisory members of the association. Now that the term of office is expiring, the executive and supervisory members should be re-elected in accordance with the regulations. Most of the executive and supervisory members have completed their four-year terms and will naturally withdraw. However, after withdrawing, no one will be in charge of the association's affairs. Are there any relief measures? Please explain the situation and request a reply. How should it be handled? Resolution: Reply to the association to handle it in accordance with the regulations of the same industry association law.

Ningbo

Dispute Arises Over Labor Service

The people of Shounan Township in Yin County began winter labor service at town construction jobs at 9:00 AM on the 10th in Zhou Su Du, south of Yin. More than 4,000 conscripted laborers arrived to attend the opening ceremony. However, after the ceremony, many of the conscripted laborers began to criticize. Troublemakers incited conflict and made things difficult for the organizers. A fashionable woman with permed hair wearing a gray tweed overcoat in the crowd even shouted for the organizers to be overthrown. A tumult arose, and order was disrupted. Mud clods and wooden sticks flew. Ni Weixiong, a section chief of the county government, technician Wang Dianzhang, and the township chiefs who were present saw that there was no reasoning and temporarily avoided the fray, and immediately telegraphed the county government to send police to suppress the crowd. However, due to time constraints, by the time the police arrived, two rooms of Township Chief Rong Gu's residence and the Daonan Elementary School building, as well as three flat rooms of the Shounan Township Office's offices and school supplies and documents, had been almost completely destroyed. Also, six rifles, four broadswords, and sixteen spears belonging to the township office were thrown into the river. Afterwards, the police apprehended more than ten people, including Lou Xiaomao, who had acted recklessly, and sent them to the Jiangshan Public Security Bureau for interrogation.

Local News

Various Circles Held Commemorative Meeting Yesterday for the 11th Anniversary of the Prime Minister's Death 78

Citywide Holiday, Flags at Half-Mast, Entertainment Suspended. The Municipal Government Held a Tree Planting Ceremony Yesterday Morning

Yesterday was the 11th anniversary of the death of Sun Yat-sen, the Prime Minister of the Kuomintang, and also Arbor Day. The municipal party headquarters specially convened representatives from all walks of life in the city at the Municipal Public Education Center at 10:00 AM to hold a commemorative meeting for the 11th anniversary of the Prime Minister's death. The municipal government also convened its subordinate agencies and schools at the auditorium at 10:00 AM to hold a tree planting ceremony. All agencies, schools, and factories were closed for one day, and all radio stations and entertainment venues were also closed for one day. Flags were flown at half-mast across the board, and military and police agencies were on alert for one day. The details are recorded as follows:

Commemorative Meeting

The commemorative meeting for the 11th anniversary of the Prime Minister's death, convened by the municipal party headquarters, was held at the Public Education Center yesterday morning at 10:00 AM, chaired by Lin Meiyan, a member of the municipal party headquarters, with Zhang Hanyun as the master of ceremonies and Du Mengsen as the recorder. The Municipal Public Security Bureau specially dispatched several police officers to maintain order at the Public Education Center. The municipal party headquarters sent several staff members to receive representatives from all walks of life in the venue.

Attending Representatives

Representatives from all walks of life who attended included: Lin Meiyan from the municipal committee, Lin Keting from the municipal women's association, Yang Dean from the New Life Movement, Wang A Jin from the fifth district's cigarette industry union, Zhao Zixiang from the Chinese Commercial Art Writers Association, He Xuniting from the first district's hydro and electrical industry union, Cen Qiyao from the steamboat industry association, Jiang Yuequan from the towing barge union, Zhao Zhenhui from the pharmaceutical industry union, Chen Peide from the Zhenjiang fellow villagers association, Wu Chunrong from the fifth district's stevedore union, Ding Zuen from the first district's cosmetics union, He Xuemin from the social affairs bureau, Xu Hongming from the toothbrush union, Zhou Xuexiang from the general labor union, Du Mengsen from the cooperative business promotion association, Cai Yiming from the elevator operator's trade union, Xu Xingjia from the health bureau, Sheng Yizhang from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs' Shanghai office, Gu Fuzhang from the Baoshan fellow villagers association, Zhang Yichen from the first special district's municipal federation, Zhang Chunyun from the fifth district's cotton spinning union, Tan Gengxin from the Shanghai Audit Office, Xu Genghua from the China National Products Maintenance Association, Zhou Yizhai from the municipal anti-smoking committee, Jin Wenyuan from the municipal agricultural association, Huang Zaoxiong from the municipal education association, Huang Xianggu, Ren Bin, and Yu Yaoqiu from the municipal party headquarters staff, and more than 300 representatives from major and minor schools and party headquarters at all levels.

Chairman's Report

After the formalities, Chairman Lin Meiyan gave a report, stating in brief: Today is the 11th anniversary of the Prime Minister's death. The Prime Minister devoted his life to the revolution, enduring great hardships. The Prime Minister still upheld his spirit of perseverance and created the Republic of China. During this commemorative occasion, we trace the Prime Minister's great revolutionary deeds and the revolutionary legacy left to us. We firmly believe that the Prime Minister is not only the highest revolutionary leader of this party but also the only revolutionary leader of the Chinese nation. However, the Prime Minister passed away in 1925, and this party lost this great revolutionary leader, and the Chinese nation also lost a respectable and lovable nanny. Now that this party has unified China, but internally the Red bandits are scurrying eastward and disturbing the west, and in some areas, they are still extremely rampant, while externally the enemies are still baring their fangs and claws, destroying our Chinese nation. The national crisis is deepening, and the nation is on the brink of danger. We firmly believe that to save this crisis, there must be a leader to succeed the Prime Minister to lead us out of this critical environment and save our people from this sea of suffering. The Prime Minister's dying words to us were: "Peace, struggle, save China." Therefore, what we hope for from this party's leader is to be able to uphold the Prime Minister's spirit and work hard to save the country. Today, the international situation is becoming increasingly tense, and we should promptly and actively prepare strategies for national survival, so as not to disappoint the Prime Minister's spirit in heaven.

Commemorative Slogans

After the Chairman's report, slogans were immediately shouted: Promote the Prime Minister's revolutionary spirit! Continue the Prime Minister's revolutionary cause!恪Strictly abide by the Prime Minister's revolutionary teachings! Step up production and construction! Commemorate the Prime Minister and strive to resist aggression and save the country! Commemorate the Prime Minister to revive the Chinese nation! Commemorate the Prime Minister to eliminate all traitors! Long live the Republic of China! Long live the Chinese Nationalist Party! Long live the Three Principles of the People!

Flags at Half-Mast to Express Grief

All party and government agencies, schools, the Jianghai Customs, state-run agencies, the Central Bank, the China Merchants Bureau, the Two Roads Administration, and central directly affiliated agencies in this city were closed for one day. All sectors flew flags at half-mast and suspended entertainment for one day to express grief. Military and police agencies also declared an alert for one day.

Tree Planting Ceremony

The municipal government held a memorial service for the anniversary of the Prime Minister's death and a tree planting ceremony at the auditorium yesterday morning at 10:00 AM. Representatives from various city agencies were present, including Ding Shuhua from the Jianghai Customs Superintendent's Office, Fan Shouzhi from the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Administration, Chen Jingzhi from the Ministry of Industry's International Trade Bureau, Cai Zengji from the state-run China Merchants Bureau, Chen Zemin from the Shanghai Audit Office, Luo Tong from the local court, Dong Chongshan from the Higher Court's Second Branch, Tang Zaili from the Third Branch, Zhang Tianfu from the First Special District Local Court, Yu Zhenhui from the Municipal Agricultural Association, Mayor Wu Tiecheng, Secretary-General Yu Hongjun, Security Chief Yang Hu, Bureau Chiefs Shen Yi, Cai Jinjun, Jiang Jianbai representing Pan Gongzhan, all officers and staff, and more than 500 students from municipal Jingye, Wuben, Xicheng, Era, Yangzheng, Feihong, Yinhang, Yanghang, Shenhang, Tangwan, and other primary and secondary schools.

Commemorative Ceremony

The presidium consisted of Mayor Wu, Secretary-General Yu, Chief Yang, Director Shen, Director Cai, and Director Pan. Mayor Wu led the ceremony: All stood at attention. Play mourning music. Sing the party song. Pay the highest respects to the party flag, the national flag, and the Prime Minister's portrait. The chairman respectfully read the Prime Minister's will. Silent tribute. Sing the tree planting song. The chairman delivers the opening speech. Tree planting. Play music and dismiss the meeting. However, due to the rain, no photos were taken.

Mayor's Speech

After the ceremony, Chairman Wu, the Mayor, delivered a speech saying: Today is the 11th anniversary of the Prime Minister's death, and we are holding a commemorative ceremony and tree planting ceremony in order to commemorate the Prime Minister's legacy of advocating afforestation. The Prime Minister said in his will that the purpose of the revolution is construction, and the most important thing in construction is people's livelihood. Therefore, the purpose of the revolution is to implement the Principle of People's Livelihood. Afforestation is the construction of the national economy, that is, the construction of people's livelihood. In recent years, our country has been plagued by frequent disasters. Both central and local authorities are actively engaged in water conservancy construction, and at the same time advocating afforestation, in order to achieve lasting stability and social livelihood. Agriculture is the foundation of our country, but the amount of agricultural imports is very large every year. The cultivation abilities inherited from the past have gradually disappeared. Therefore, in order to save the country and seek national prosperity, we must implement the Principle of People's Livelihood. As the ancient saying goes, "It takes ten years to grow a tree, but a hundred years to cultivate a man." All of you children who are participating in the ceremony today must understand this principle. To be a human being, one must first receive good education from the country, society, and family, acquire sufficient knowledge, and contribute to society and the country in order to exert the ability to be a human being. Only then will life have value.

Tree Planting

Immediately afterward, they went to the front of the municipal government to plant trees. Dozens of cypresses were planted along the road. On the left were the Mayor, the Secretary-General, the Security Chief, the Director of the Social Affairs Bureau, the Director of the Two Roads Bureau, the Director of the Education Bureau, the Director of the Public Security Bureau, the Director of the Land Bureau, the Director of the Public Works Bureau, the Director of the Health Bureau, and the Director of the Public Utilities Bureau. On the right were the Municipal Party Headquarters, the Municipal Assembly, the New Life Movement Promotion Association, the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, the Municipal Federation of Trade Unions, the Municipal Education Association, the Municipal Agricultural Association, and the Municipal Defense Committee. Led by Mayor Wu, they braved the rain on the roadside, holding iron shovels, and personally planted the trees. The ceremony ended at 11:00 AM.

Two Roads Commemoration

Yesterday was the 11th anniversary of the death of the Prime Minister. The Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Special Party Headquarters and the Two Roads Administration jointly held a commemorative meeting and tree planting ceremony at the Shanghai West Railway Station. More than 400 representatives attended that day. Chairman Chen Chengshi respectfully read the Prime Minister's will. Yang Youren from the Party Headquarters and the Secretary of the Railway Bureau presented wreaths. Wang Cheng read the eulogy. Director Huang Boqiao then reported on the significance of commemorating the Prime Minister's death and the importance of the afforestation movement, and the points that colleagues of this road should pay attention to in tree planting. Then, Committee Member Chen Chengshi gave a speech on "Peace, Struggle, Save China" and the essentials for comrades and colleagues to deal with the national crisis, called out slogans, and then the whole group took a photo and planted trees together.

County Government Tree Planting

City Health Bureau Director Li Tingan Returned to China Yesterday 79

Resumes Duty Today

Report to the Capital in the Coming Days

Mr. Li Tingan, the Director of the Municipal Health Bureau of this city, was ordered to go abroad in early November of last year to inspect health administration affairs in Europe and the United States. After spending four months and visiting more than ten countries, he arrived in Shanghai yesterday afternoon on the Norddeutscher Lloyd's Scharnhorst. The ship docked at the Gonghexiang Wharf at 4:00 PM, and all the welcoming personnel boarded the ship to shake hands and greet Mr. Li. He then disembarked and returned to his residence in Shanghai.

Inspection Process

The Central News Agency reporter met with Mr. Li on the ship. According to him, he was ordered to go abroad for inspection and visited more than ten countries. He first went to Japan, then crossed the Pacific Ocean to Canada and the United States. Then he crossed the Atlantic Ocean to the United Kingdom, the Netherlands, Denmark, Germany, Poland, Czechoslovakia, Yugoslavia, Switzerland, Italy, and other countries. In Geneva, he met with Dr. Rajchman, the former League of Nations technical expert sent to China, to exchange ideas on improving China's health administration.

Impressions

During this trip, I visited Japan and various European and American countries. My impression is that all countries are striving to update their health facilities, and there are many improvements in health administration that can be used as a model for our country. Among them, Yugoslavia's health administration is particularly suitable for China's national conditions. Therefore, in the future, I plan to use Yugoslavia's health administration as the basis for reforming China's health administration.

Resumes Duty Today

Mr. Li has been away from the country for a long time, and all important bureau affairs need to be handled personally. Therefore, he will resume duty today. All health facilities in this city are being actively improved, and various health construction projects are being actively undertaken. The opening of municipal hospitals, the expansion of health offices and health laboratories in various districts, and the development of various other health affairs all await Mr. Li's planning.

Visit to the Mayor

Mr. Li was sent abroad by the Municipal Government and the Central Health Administration to inspect the health administration of various countries. Therefore, he will visit Mayor Wu Tiecheng today to report on the inspection process, so that the capital city can learn from it in developing health undertakings. He will also go to the capital in the coming days to report to Liu Ruiheng, the Director of the Health Administration. As for Mr. Li's detailed report on his overseas inspection, it will be published after it has been organized.

To handle embassy affairs for two weeks, then south

After bidding farewell to the authorities, he will return to his country

As his departure from China is imminent, he, along with his staff, took the Shanghai-Peiping through train yesterday afternoon at 4 PM to head north to Peiping to handle embassy affairs. The Economic Commission and Anhui Provincial Government Deny Controlling Qihong Tea 84

The Shanghai Tea Association Received a Reply Telegram Yesterday

The National News Agency reported that the foreign tea firms in Shanghai, after hearing rumors that the National Economic Commission was going to control Qihong black tea, telegraphed the relevant authorities to express their opposition. The association yesterday received a letter and telegram from the National Economic Commission and the Anhui Provincial Government forwarded by the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce, stating that such rumors were a misunderstanding and not factual. The letter and telegram are recorded below:

Anhui Provincial Government Telegram: In direct reply, regarding the telegram arguing against the control of Qihong tea, we previously received a reply telegram from the National Economic Commission and have already forwarded it to your association. Now, on the 4th of this month, we received another telegram from Chairman Liu of the Anhui Provincial Government and the Deputy Director of the Construction Department, stating, "We acknowledge receipt of the telegram. This was decided at the Qihong Tea Technology Discussion Conference of the National Economic Commission, which only discussed the marketing methods of Qihong black tea and did not decide to control Qihong tea. Even the marketing methods are still under careful discussion and will not hinder tea firms from making loans. Please inform them not to worry too much." This telegram has been received. A corresponding letter is hereby sent to you for your information. Addressed to: Foreign Tea Firms Association of Shanghai, Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce.

Economic Commission Letter: In direct reply, on the 2nd of this month, the Secretariat of the National Economic Commission approved Document No. 22109 of the Agriculture Department, stating, "We acknowledge receipt of the telegram. The purpose of the Agriculture Department convening the Tea Technology Discussion Conference is to improve Chinese tea, not to control Qihong tea. Although a representative from the Anhui Construction Department proposed Qihong tea marketing methods, after extensive discussion, only the principles were approved, with the caveat that export tea merchants (i.e., tea firms facing unemployment and debt) must be considered. The conference had already taken the position of the tea firms into account. In summary, the Agriculture Department of the Commission has always held the principle of cooperation and mutual assistance to revitalize Chinese tea. Although there were many advocates for control at the time of the discussion, the conference believed that this matter was of great importance, and the purpose of the conference was to focus on technical research. It treated all sectors of the tea industry equally, considered all aspects, and did not discriminate. The Foreign Tea Firms Association had previously telegraphed Mr. Zhou to express their thanks, and we have already sent a detailed reply. We are now sending another telegram for your information." Approved. We have received your association's letter regarding this case and have forwarded it for investigation and reply. The reply is now approved. Please inform them accordingly. Addressed to: Foreign Tea Firms Association of Shanghai, Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce.

Shaanxi Provincial Government Borrowed 240,000 Yuan From the Three Banks 85

Using 400,000 Yuan in Central Government Bonds for Disaster Relief in Shaanxi as Collateral

The Term is Six Months and the Contract Was Signed in Xi'an

After receiving 500,000 yuan in disaster relief bonds from the central government, the Shaanxi Provincial Government negotiated with the Xi'an branches of the Shanghai Central Bank of China, Bank of China, and Bank of Communications to mortgage them for cash. The New News Agency reporter learned from banking circles yesterday morning that after initial consultations in Xi'an, Yan Jingzhai came to Shanghai to negotiate with the three banks. As a result, it was decided to mortgage 400,000 yuan of bonds at 60% for 240,000 yuan in cash. The Central Bank of China, Bank of China, and Bank of Communications will lend according to a 4:4:2 ratio, with the Central Bank of China and Bank of China each contributing 96,000 yuan and the Bank of Communications contributing 48,000 yuan. The term is six months, with an interest rate of 8%. The loan contract will be signed in Xi'an, and the Xi'an branches of the Central Bank of China, Bank of China, and Bank of Communications will disburse the funds nearby. The remaining 100,000 yuan in bonds will be mortgaged to local banks in Shaanxi to provide relief to disaster victims in northern Shaanxi.

Zhu Qinglan, Chairman of the National Government's Relief Committee, took an early train from Shanghai to Zhenjiang on the 11th to discuss disaster relief matters. He is scheduled to return to Shanghai on the evening of the 12th. After returning to Shanghai, Zhu plans to stay for a few days to discuss disaster relief matters with various circles in Shanghai, and then he will go to Nanking with Tang Zongguo and other members of the Relief Committee to inspect disaster relief efforts in Henan and Shanxi.
