The Premier's ideology is the ideology of saving the country. We must practice the Three Principles of the People in order to achieve the goal of saving the country. The local products movement is part of the movement to save the country. To save the country, we must first be prepared, militarily and even more so economically. Promoting local products is to strengthen economic power.

Speech by Zhang Yuanruo

Zhang Yuanruo, representing Mayor Wu, said in his speech that all Chinese people need to revive the nation, but the revival of the nation requires practical work, which cannot be achieved by empty talk. The most important task is to strengthen national power. National power has many aspects, the most important of which is economic power. The basic significance of the local products movement lies in strengthening economic power and developing the nation's productive forces. Finally, he hoped that local product producers would strive for excellence day by day, so that local products could occupy a place in the world market. He hoped that consumers would not wait until local products were improved before using them. At present, we can only simplify our lives and use local products.

Speech by Jiang Wenbao

Jiang Wenbao, representing Education Bureau Director Pan Gongzhan, said in his speech that people's lives all aspire to improvement, but now is a time of national crisis and a time for the people to endure hardship. We should not only think about enjoyment, but should cultivate a spirit of hard work and endurance. Promoting local products can also cure China's poverty and weakness and save the nation's economic power. Speeches were also given by Zhang Jingye, representing the Shanghai County Party Headquarters, Xu Genghua from the China National Products Maintenance Association, and guest Chen Jicheng. The speeches were omitted for brevity.

Implementation Outline

The implementation outline of the first year of the local products promotion plan is as follows: (A) Regarding investigation: Investigate famous local products in various places, investigate improved local products in various places, investigate the production and sales situation, investigate the socio-economic situation; (B) Regarding improvement: Promote superior varieties of crops, improve handicraft weaving, improve animal husbandry, promote agricultural product manufacturing; (C) Regarding promotion: Hold lectures, hold promotion weeks, compile and publish publications, hold exhibitions; (D) Regarding implementation: Introduce superior local products, promote production and marketing cooperatives, provide small loans, reward the use of local products.

The Four Banks Separately Receive the Preparations of the Provincial Banks 89

The preparations of the eight banks in this city have been received clearly

The National News Agency reported that the Issuance Preparation Committee of the Ministry of Finance has entrusted the four banks, namely the Central Bank of China, Bank of China, Bank of Communications, and Farmers Bank of China, to receive the cash reserves and guarantee reserves of various banks inside and outside this city. The provincial and local banks have now been assigned to the four banks for separate receipt. The banks in this city have been received clearly, and only minor issues remain to be resolved in accordance with the ministry's order. The details are recorded below:

Two Methods Determined for Receiving

Before the Farmers Bank of China obtained the right of issuance, the provincial and local banks were first received jointly by the Central Bank of China, Bank of China, and Bank of Communications. However, due to the relationship of joint receipt, everything, big or small, had to be discussed by the three banks before it could be carried out, which was not unified in authority and not economical in time. Therefore, the Issuance Preparation Committee decided on two new methods yesterday: The provincial and local banks that have already been received by the Central Bank of China, Bank of China, and Bank of Communications will continue to be received by the three banks, but they will be assigned separately, each receiving one or several banks. The provincial and local banks that have not yet been received will be entrusted to the Farmers Bank of China for receipt in order to unify authority and facilitate prompt action.

Methods for Distributing Banks Already Received

As for the provincial and local banks that have already been jointly received by the Central Bank of China, Bank of China, and Bank of Communications, the method of assigning receipt is based on the depth of the mutual relationship between the banks, as follows: (A) The Central Bank of China receives the Shaanxi Provincial Bank; (B) The Bank of China receives the Peiping Baoshang Bank, the Zhejiang Local Bank, and the Henan Agricultural and Industrial Bank; (C) The Bank of Communications receives the Hubei Provincial Bank, the Tianjin Bianye Bank, and the Dazhong Bank, which moved its head office from Tianjin to Shanghai.

Receipt of the Eight Banks in This City is Clear

The Central Bank of China, Bank of China, and Bank of Communications received the cash reserves and guarantee reserves of the eight banks that issue banknotes (originally nine banks, but the Farmers Bank of China has now been specially licensed by the government to issue banknotes). Except for minor issues such as the banknotes of the branches of the eight banks in other cities being exchanged for cash at the three banks whenever they are transported to Shanghai, the rest has been received clearly. As for the new banknotes that have been printed but not yet issued by the eight banks, except for the new banknotes of the China Agricultural and Industrial Bank which will be overprinted and issued by the Central Bank of China, and the new banknotes of the China Industrial Bank which will be overprinted and issued by the Bank of Communications, there are many new banknotes of other banks that have been printed but not yet issued. How to dispose of them has been communicated by the three banks to the Issuance Preparation Committee and forwarded to the Ministry of Finance for review and decision. The new banknotes of each bank are still sealed and awaiting orders.

Ministry Approved National Federation of Commerce Requests Shandong Fishery Salt Exempted from Color Change 90

Wang Guan Chang is an inland river fishery and should still be used

Shenshi News Agency reported that the National Federation of Chambers of Commerce, at the request of Rongcheng County, Shandong, sent a telegram to the Ministry of Finance on October 25 last year, stating that changing the color of fishery salt would hinder the fishing industry and requesting exemption from color change. The Federation has received a reply from the Ministry of Finance stating, "We acknowledge receipt of the telegram. Regarding the case of using red soil to change the color of fishery salt in the Shandong area, the Shandong Rongcheng County Chamber of Commerce and others previously submitted a petition to the ministry, stating that using red soil to change the color of fishery salt would affect the sales of fish and requesting permission to use white salt as before. After verification, it was found that except for Wang Guan Chang fishery salt in the Shandong area, which is an inland river fishery used for pickling shrimp paste, which should still be used and the color should still be changed with red soil as before, the other fishery salt farms do not need to implement the color change for the time being in order to avoid disturbances. Separate instructions have been issued to the relevant departments to comply with the above. Please be informed of the above information. This approval."

Shanghai Commercial & Savings Bank Promotes Acceptance Bills 91

And Offers Discounting, Welcoming Inquiries from All Sectors

Dagong News Agency reported that Shanghai Commercial & Savings Bank has recently been striving to promote acceptance bills in order to circulate the market and aid industry and commerce. It has specially formulated nine measures to welcome inquiries from all sectors for handling. The measures announced by the bank are listed below: The bank handles acceptance and discounting of bills of exchange in order to serve the society and assist industrial and commercial enterprises. Any company or firm that has been issued an export bill of exchange by the bank or has entered into an acceptance agreement with the bank may issue a bill of exchange payable by the bank within the scope of the agreement, and the bank will accept it. The acceptance fee is determined by the bank at 1/10 of a percent of the face amount. The term of any bill of exchange accepted by the bank is limited to 120 days. Any bank acceptance bill or commercial acceptance bill approved by the bank may be discounted. Commercial acceptance bills are limited to those arising from genuine goods transactions. The discount rate may be determined by the bank at any time. If a bill of exchange discounted by the bank is not paid upon maturity, the drawer, endorser, acceptor, and guarantor shall be jointly and severally liable. The bank may amend these regulations at any time.

Japanese Set Up Ramie Spinning Mills in Korea to Resist Our Summer Cloth 94

Consul in Korea Recently Reported to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs

Urging Our Summer Cloth Industry Merchants to Pay Attention

Shenshi News Agency reported that the Ministry of Foreign Affairs recently received a report from the consulate in Korea that the famous summer cloth produced in our country is imported into Korea every year, reaching more than 10 million bolts with a total value of 6 million yuan. Since Korea increased tariffs in 1920, there have also been about 1 million bolts. Unexpectedly, in the past two or three years, it has decreased sharply. The amount imported into Korea last year was only about one-tenth of what it used to be, only about 100,000 bolts. The reason for this is that Korea raised tariffs again in 1932. It was recently learned that Kanebo Textiles, a Japanese company, is planning to establish the world's only ramie spinning factory in Daejeon, Chungcheongnam-do, Korea. It has purchased 200,000 ping of land for the site and is engaged in construction. It has also transported 2 million ramie plants from Taiwan, planning to complete the project within three years. In addition to meeting the needs of all Korean people, it can also manufacture various ramie yarns and ramie cloths and extend its sales to various countries. In the future, our summer cloth industry will not only have its sales to Korea completely wiped out, but also be eliminated by Japanese summer cloth due to heavy tariffs and uneven quality and length of cloth. Therefore, it is proposed that the Ministry of Foreign Affairs should forward this information to the Ministry of Industry to instruct merchants engaged in the summer cloth industry in our country to pay close attention in order to save the situation.

The Third National Congress of the National Postal Workers' Union Will Open on the 15th 95

Representatives from All Over Have Reported In

More Than Two Hundred Proposals Received

Dagon News Agency reported that the National Postal Workers' Union of the Republic of China is organized by postal workers' unions from all over the country. It was established in 1929. According to the union's constitution, a national congress of representatives is convened every two years. The first congress was held in Shanghai in December 1929, and the second congress was held in the capital in 1931. The third congress failed to be convened as scheduled due to various reasons. The 23rd Standing Committee meeting of the union has resolved that it will be held in Shanghai starting on March 15. As the opening date is approaching, preparations are in full swing, and representatives from all over have reported in. Details are explored as follows:

Organization of the Congress: The National Congress of Representatives is organized by representatives legally elected by postal workers' unions from all over the country. Any union with fewer than 300 members may elect one representative, those with 300 to 1,000 members may elect two representatives, those with 1,000 to 2,000 members may elect three representatives, and those with more than 2,000 members may elect four representatives. The executive and supervisory committee members of the National Postal Workers' Union may attend the opening of the Congress. The supervisory committee members may attend the presidium of the Congress, which consists of five people elected by the Congress. The Congress has a secretariat to handle all matters under the direction of the presidium of the Congress.

Staff of the Congress: The Congress has a secretariat, with the following personnel: Secretary-General Zhao Shusheng, Secretaries Xiao Qingshan, Chen Shigao, Zhang Guangdai, Kong Fanzao, Head of the Document Section Zhang Zuoqi, Document Staff Gu Xizhang, Shi Jiuyuan, Head of the Accounting Section Fan Caicong, Accountant Xiao Pusong, Head of the Reception Section Cheng Zuoqing, Reception Staff Shui Xiangyun, Lu Keming, Wang Kai, Liu Xinquan, Wang Zhenbai, Xu Duowu, Ya Xiong, Zou Zhipeng, Head of the Affairs Section Zhang Da, Affairs Staff Shen Jizhou, Yang Delin, Chen Jinbao, Zheng Wenquan, Wu Tinglun.

Representatives Reporting In: Representatives from postal workers' unions all over the country have enthusiastically reported to this Congress. As of yesterday, representatives from Shanghai, Zhejiang, Yantai, Wujin, Fuzhou, Shantou, Sichuan, Tongshan, Qingdao, Guangzhou, Nanchang, Ningbo, Wuxi, Changsha, Xiamen, Suzhou, Huaining, Luoyang, Jinan, Zhenjiang, Tianjin, Jiujiang, Wuhu, Hankou, Yunnan, Nanking, Kaifeng, Zheng County, Jiangdu, Changde, and other places have reported in, totaling over 100 people.

Reception: The Congress reception is located at the New Zha Hotel on the third floor at the intersection of New Zha Road and Card Road. The entire third floor is rented for the accommodation of representatives. Representatives arriving in Shanghai are met at the docks and train stations by staff from the Congress' reception section. As of yesterday, representatives from Changsha (two), Fuzhou (four), Yantai (one), Hankou (one), Changde (one), Hangzhou (four), and Jiangdu (one) had arrived in Shanghai. Representatives from other places will arrive in succession within one or two days.

A Glimpse of the Proposals: The Congress secretariat has now received over 200 proposals from unions across the country. The contents of the proposals can be roughly divided into five categories: Matters concerning the transformation of bureau affairs, suggestions concerning union affairs, matters concerning the promotion of member welfare, matters concerning the improvement of postal bureau treatment, and general matters concerning national economy and people's livelihood.

Shanghai Parents Education Research Association Held Its Ninth Regular Meeting Yesterday 98

Su Zengxiang Gave a Lecture on Children's Tuberculosis

Hu Zuyin Elaborated on the Mechanism of Children's Behavior

The Shanghai Parents Education Research Association held its ninth regular meeting at Hu's residence in Pingliang Village, Pingliang Road, at 6:30 pm yesterday. Members Zhu Duanfang, Liao Jiayi, Gu Jingren, Zhang Liling, Li Jingde, Wang Liufen, Hu Zuyin, Tao Shaoyuan, Ge Liting, Zhao Chuanjia, Mei Jinliang, Zhang Shizhang, Chen Hanming, Chen Zhengfan, and specially invited pediatric expert Su Zengxiang, who studied in Germany, attended. After dinner, Su Zengxiang first gave a lecture on children's tuberculosis, saying that children's tuberculosis is by no means hereditary but arises from various acquired causes, such as contact with patients, hugging and kissing adults, drinking unsterilized milk, and parents taking them to dirty public places. Prevention methods focus on three major conditions: sunlight, air, and cod liver oil. When studying in Germany, she saw newborn babies in that country lying in nurseries with open windows and circulating air, even in snowy weather. Their bodies were covered with extremely warm blankets, with their mouths and noses fully exposed. Hot water bottles and electric heaters were placed beside them to increase the heat. This method can be used for reference by parents in our country. Then, Hu Zuyin elaborated on the mechanisms of children's behavior, roughly divided into identification, compensation, transfer, regression, rationalization, suppression, projection, escape, and self-defense reactions. In general, behavioral mechanisms are mechanical movements in behavior, representing various methods for people to cope with the environment. If parents can understand the various behavioral mechanisms of children, it will be easier to guide and manage them. Finally, Chairman Zhu Duanfang reported on the association's affairs. Member Chen Zhengfan has recently completed a book entitled "The Road of Chinese Parents," which is scheduled to be published on Children's Day this year and dedicated to parents across the country. The book's content includes: The Song of Chinese Parents, The Road of Chinese Parents, Chinese Parents in Extraordinary Times, Inspiration from the Souls of War Heroes, Ten Commandments for Parents, Intelligence Tests for Parents, Standards for Family Education, An Overview of Children's Health Science, An Introduction to Twenty Famous Works on Parents Education, The Soviet Mother-Child Competition, French Parents' Life, Notes for Mothers, and Notes for Infant Care. The author's purpose is to destroy the familyism of the East and replace it with collectivism, hoping to transform the psychology of ordinary parents and enable them to change their ways, work hard, and keep pace with the parents of modern civilized countries. It is expected that once this book is published, its impact on the future of our society will be far-reaching. The China Child Welfare Association is scheduled to convene the Second National Child Welfare Conference in Qingdao, Shandong, from July 14 to 18 this year. Our association, as one of the child welfare organizations, has received informal notice that in the future, in addition to sending representatives to participate in the conference, we must also prepare papers on parents' education to be presented and read at the conference. After the chairman's report, several motions were passed, and the meeting was adjourned, already at 9:30 pm.

The names of the member silk mills are "XXX United Silk Manufacturing Industry XXX Silk Mill." They strive to improve the quality of their products to compete with foreign silk in the European and American markets, with the aim of saving the declining Chinese silk industry.

The Route Was Not Wrong Wang Jinfa Commits Manslaughter

The entire family's livelihood depended on him. Now that he has been tragically crushed to death, the entire family's life is in a desperate situation. Gao Wu Abuses Adopted Daughter Dongying Suffers Injuries All Over Her Body 105

Her Husband Argues Ineffectively, Reports the Case, and the Defendant Is Arrested and Admits the Crime, Sentencing Is Scheduled

Hu Fuying, a native of Hubei, due to poverty, adopted out her four-year-old daughter Dongying to a fellow villager, Gao Wu, a housewife residing in a bungalow in Caoxiebang, Gordon Road, West Shanghai, on November 6 of last year. At that time, in addition to a written agreement, Hu also gave a dowry of 12 yuan. However, Gao Wu was by nature violent. After Dongying entered her home, she abused her, using the excuse that Dongying did not know how to be clean and made a mess with urine and feces, often whipping her. In addition to pressing her fingernails all over her body, she also used iron needles to prick the palms of both her hands, causing Dongying to be injured all over her body in a few months, and her cries were incessant. Nearby neighbors could not bear it and gossiped about it. Hu Fuying, Dongying's biological father, heard about it and went to Gao Wu's house to investigate. He found Dongying's face pale and her body full of injuries. When he argued with Gao, she was stubborn and unreasonable. Seeing that she could not be reasoned with, Hu went outside and called Chinese police officer No. 671, who arrested Gao Wu and took her to the Putuo Road Police Station, which transferred her to the women's prison for detention. He sent Dongying to Guangren Hospital, where it was confirmed that she had scars all over her body and two needle pricks on the palms of both hands. He issued an injury certificate and handed it over to the police station for filing. Gao Wu was sent to the First Special Court the day before yesterday, and prosecuted under Article 286, Paragraph 1 of the Criminal Code for the crime of injury. Police lawyer Zhang Tianyin stated the case, saying that when he went to arrest the defendant yesterday, the neighbors all said that they often heard the defendant beat Dongying. This kind of fierce and evil person should be arrested. Dongying has also been brought to court. He presented the injury certificate to the court. According to Dongying's testimony, she was beaten and pricked with needles by the defendant, and Judge Liu verified in court that there were black dots and many scars on the palms of Dongying's hands. When questioned, Gao Wu admitted that because Dongying did not know how to be clean and often urinated on her pants, she beat her four times with her hands and pricked her once with a needle. Judge Liu ordered that the debate in this case be concluded and the sentence be announced next Wednesday. Gao Wu was remanded in custody, and Dongying was examined by the court's forensic doctor and taken back by her father, Hu Fuying.

Two Buildings Built on Leased Land, Listed at 5,013 Yuan, Bidding Opens on the 14th in the Morning

Datong News Agency reports that since the China Public Huang Automobile Company ceased operations last year, the Second Special Court, at the request of creditors, ruled the company bankrupt. The minimum price was assessed and auctioned once, but no one bid. The highest bidder will be awarded the bid on the day of the bidding and will pay the price and take over the property. Le Shinong Talks About the Successful Development of Cigarette Paper 110

Perseverance Pays Off

The China Cigarette Paper Manufacturing Co., Ltd. has completely succeeded in researching and manufacturing cigarette surface paper, which is expected to reduce leakage by more than 4 million yuan annually. A reporter from the Shanghai News Agency specially visited Le Shinong, the assistant manager of the company, yesterday to inquire about the imitation process.

Ten Years of Research and Development

The factory director, Ge Tianmin, had a close relationship with Mr. Zengai Tatsusaburo, a famous Japanese cigarette paper manufacturer, during his stay in Japan. Over tea and wine, they discussed the raw materials and manufacturing methods. Over the years, he learned a lot. He also sent his relative Hong Shaoting to work as a laborer in the Kitagawa Paper Mill for as long as ten years, observing and working hard, and deeply understanding the manufacturing method. Unable to endure any longer, he purchased a machine and returned to China last year to set up a factory to imitate the product. After one year of improvement, he succeeded.

Official Shipment

The factory has now raised a capital of 100,000 yuan and purchased a large machine specially for making cigarette paper from abroad. Together with the old one, there are two machines in total, which are currently in production. However, due to registration procedures, it is not easy to complete for the time being. According to Article 1 of the Regulations for Encouraging Industry promulgated by the Ministry of Industry, this invention of the factory should, as a rule, obtain the exclusive manufacturing right for ten years or less for sales throughout the country. In addition to sending personnel to Beijing to apply for awards from the Minister of Industry, it is heard that the factory is striving for scientific organization. According to Mr. Le, the factory is currently preparing for safety equipment, hygiene equipment, and simple life insurance for workers, with an annual budget of no less than several thousand yuan.

Recovering Leakage

Although cigarette paper is an extremely small item, the annual consumption is extremely large because many Chinese people like to smoke. According to Chinese cigarette factories, the annual output of cigarettes reaches one million boxes, and each box requires one roll of cigarette paper. Therefore, the annual consumption of cigarette paper also needs one million rolls. However, in fact, the factory does not have such a large output because its scope is limited, and the two machines cannot meet the demand. This is an inevitable trend in the future. Recently, many cigarette factories in Japan and other foreign countries have requested samples from the factory. However, because the factory's issuance procedures are not well-arranged, it has not been able to meet the expectations of all sectors for the time being.

The First Special Court Complies with Orders to Stipulate Eight-Hour Workdays 117

Staff Must Sign in Before 8 A.M.

In order to increase administrative efficiency, the central government issued a circular to all agencies inside and outside the capital, stipulating that daily working hours should be eight hours. The Shanghai First Special District Local Court has now complied with this directive and has changed its daily working hours to start at 8 a.m. and end at 12 p.m., and then from 2 p.m. to 6 p.m. On the first day of implementation (last Friday), Court President Guo Yunguan, in order to set an example for his subordinates, should set an example himself. Therefore, after 7 a.m., he arrived at the court and signed in first. By 8 a.m., the prepared sign-in book had been sent to the Court President's office, so staff who arrived at the court slightly later were unable to sign in. However, from the second day onwards, everyone arrived at the court on time.

Since the Shanghai Telephone Company implemented a per-call charging system, it has been very difficult for litigants in various courts in this city to use the telephone when they encounter urgent matters. Therefore, the Shanghai Lawyers Association, in order to facilitate lawyers and litigants, has proposed a joint meeting of the Executive and Supervisory Committees, which resolved to send a letter to various courts in this city, requesting the installation of public telephones specifically for the use of lawyers and litigants. The Public Bus Company in the International Settlement's Revised Fare Regulations Approved by the Engineering Bureau 121

The Continental News reports that the Public Bus Company in the International Settlement has revised its fare regulations due to the use of new fractional currency in China. It is said that it has been approved by the Engineering Bureau. According to an employee of the company, the new regulations can now be implemented, but because the daily revenue of new fractional currency is only about 250 yuan, it is planned to implement the new regulations after the revenue greatly increases. It is expected that the increase will be gradual. The Public Works Department fully approved the new regulations submitted by the company this time, without making any modifications. The new regulations do not increase the fare. The new fractional currency is equivalent to three old copper coins, and the current fare is not divided by "three", so it has to be revised. Some of the fares are slightly increased, and some are slightly reduced. For example, the fare for Route 1, which is ten cents, has to be changed to nine cents, which is equivalent to three new fractional currency. However, in order to compensate for the loss of income, the two fares are calculated based on the converted new fractional currency, which has slightly increased. The company predicted several weeks ago that the new regulations could be implemented on March 1, but based on the current situation, it is not likely to be implemented in the near future. The implementation of the new regulations will inevitably be a bit troublesome at the beginning. Therefore, the managers hope to implement them after the new fractional currency is widely used. The new fractional currency is indeed more convenient than the old copper coins. It is lighter and easier for passengers to carry, and it can also reduce the weight on the ticket seller's shoulders by two-thirds. Although the company currently only receives 250 yuan of new fractional currency per day, the number is still small, but it has increased compared to several weeks ago, which proves that the number of users has gradually increased.

Cai Zengji Discusses the Reorganization of the China Merchants Bureau's Debts, Rumors Are Not True 124

Central News Agency reports that reporter met Cai Zengji, the Director-General of the state-owned China Merchants Bureau, at the Municipal Government yesterday to discuss the issue of reorganizing the old debts of the Bureau. According to him, the Bureau is currently studying a fundamental solution to the reorganization of old debts in detail. After the plan is drafted and submitted to the central government for approval, it will be published in writing. This matter is of great importance and cannot be announced casually orally. As for the amount of old debts, he said that the total amount of principal and interest is about 39 million yuan. Among them, the principal and interest owed to the British HSBC Bank is about 13 million yuan, and the principal and interest owed to the American Citibank is about 1.5 million yuan. The remaining debts are owed to domestic banks and money shops, and a small part is for guarantees and employees' savings. Therefore, the content is very complex. The foreign debt part is related to China's foreign debt credibility and diplomatic issues between China and the creditor countries, as well as financial issues. The domestic debt part is also of great importance to the domestic economy, social finance, and the government's credibility to the people. However, in any case, the most reasonable and fair principles will be followed in the future, and the economic, diplomatic, and credit relations of all parties, as well as the economic capabilities and shipping plans of the China Merchants Bureau itself, will be taken into consideration, and detailed measures will be formulated to seek a thorough solution. Cai concluded that since the relations of this matter are as complex as described above, it will take a considerable amount of time to study and agree on it.

All Parties Support and Unanimously Promote Commercial Ethics, China-China Silk and Satin Company Takes the Lead and Loudly Calls for Action 125

Trustworthiness is the foundation of commercial ethics, hence the ancient Chinese saying "Trustworthiness leads to commerce." However, in recent years, due to fierce commercial competition, most people only seek immediate benefits and disregard their own credibility. Furthermore, there is a lot of infighting and jealousy among peers. The two words "trustworthiness" are no longer valued by merchants today, and commercial ethics have been completely destroyed. The China-China Silk and Satin Company, in view of this, deeply feels that it is necessary to improve commercial ethics in order to achieve the permanent survival of various industries. Therefore, it sent a letter to the Silk and Satin Industry Association of this city the day before yesterday, requesting that it forward the letter to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce. On the one hand, it should persuade all industries to establish a unified market price, create mutually beneficial industry rules, and jointly abide by them. On the other hand, it should submit a request to the government authorities to take concrete and effective measures to ban exaggerated and false advertisements and broadcasts that undermine commercial peers and damage commercial ethics. In this way, a permanent foundation can be established for the future of industry and commerce. It is heard that after the China-China Company issued the letter, the Silk and Satin Industry Association forwarded it to the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce. The Chamber of Commerce is also considering implementation measures, and industry leaders are also paying close attention to it. Therefore, the promotion of commercial ethics may become a new movement in the industrial and commercial sectors. (The original letter from China-China Silk and Satin Company to the Silk and Satin Industry Association has been seen in yesterday's newspaper and is omitted here.)

The Guhua Vase Case Overturns the Original Verdict, Jiang Yuting is Innocent 133

Chi Yunfei's private prosecution against Jiang Yuting, the manager of Yuanzhang Jewelry Store on Shanxi Road, for defrauding him of a Guyuexuan vase, Jiang Yuting was previously sentenced to eight months in prison with a two-year suspension by the First Special District Local Court. Because Jiang Yuting was dissatisfied, he still hired lawyer Lu Shaozong and others to appeal to the Second Branch of the Jiangsu High Court. The plaintiff, Chi Yunfei, also filed an appeal because the sentence for Jiang Yuting in the first instance was too light. After deliberation by Judge Yu and the two judges, Zhou and Zhong, the verdict was announced on the same day, the original verdict was overturned, Jiang Yuting was found not guilty, and Chi Yunfei's appeal was rejected. The case of the ancient vase, which had been widely publicized for a time, has finally come to an end.

Weather Report 144

The Xujiahui Observatory's meteorological forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday stated that the weather around Shandong is cold, with snowfall, and there are strong northeasterly winds. The Yangtze River Basin is overcast, with rain or snow, and there is a gradual appearance of fog. The wind comes from the northwest to northeast and there is fog. There are cyclones, rain, or fog in the Yellow Sea and the East China Sea, caused by low pressure passing and moving towards the northeast. There is fog around Taiwan, and the wind direction is uncertain. Also, in the 24 hours before 3:00 PM yesterday, the temperature in the city was 46.6 degrees at the highest and 43.3 degrees at the lowest. On the same day last year, the highest was 73.8 degrees and the lowest was 39.2 degrees.

Education News

Promulgation of Revised Organizational Regulations and Qualification Review Regulations for Deans of Students and Civic Education Teachers 146

The Ministry of Education Orders All Provinces and Cities to Comply

The Ministry of Education issued a circular to the education departments of all provinces and cities on the 11th, stating, "In accordance with the Executive Yuan's Instruction No. 1359 of March 4, 1936, which states, 'In accordance with the National Government's Instruction No. 239 of March 3, 1936, which states, "In accordance with the Central Executive Committee's letter of February 27, 1936, "After reviewing the Regulations for the Examination of Qualifications of Civic Education Teachers in Secondary Schools and the Regulations for the Examination of Qualifications of Deans of Students in Secondary Schools passed by the 86th Standing Committee of the Third Central Committee, it was found that there were several points that needed to be revised. Moreover, the two regulations are similar in nature and should be merged to demonstrate orderliness. Therefore, a new set of Regulations for the Examination of Qualifications of Deans of Students and Civic Education Teachers in Secondary Schools has been drafted, and the Organizational Regulations for the Committee for the Examination of Qualifications of Deans of Students and Civic Education Teachers has been slightly revised. These were submitted to and approved by the Sixth Meeting of the Standing Committee of this Committee. All previously promulgated Regulations for the Examination of Qualifications of Civic Education Teachers in Secondary Schools and Regulations for the Examination of Qualifications of Deans of Students in Secondary Schools should be abolished immediately. In addition to issuing a circular to the Party headquarters of all provinces and cities to comply with, we are hereby enclosing the Regulations for the Examination of Qualifications of Deans of Students and Civic Education Teachers in Secondary Schools and the Revised Organizational Regulations for the Committee for the Examination of Qualifications of Deans of Students and Civic Education Teachers for your reference and transmission to the relevant agencies for compliance."' Therefore, we should comply. In addition to replying to the letter, we are hereby enclosing the original regulations and ordering your Ministry to comply with them."' Therefore, we are hereby copying and issuing the original regulations, ordering you to comply with them and instructing your subordinates to comply with them in full. This order is issued."

Regulations for the Examination of Qualifications of Deans of Students and Civic Education Teachers in Secondary Schools 147

(Passed by the Sixth Meeting of the Fifth Central Standing Committee on February 20, 1936)

Article 1 The examination of the qualifications of deans of students and civic education teachers in secondary schools nationwide shall be conducted by the Committee for the Examination of Qualifications of Deans of Students and Civic Education Teachers in accordance with these regulations. The organization of the Committee for the Examination of Qualifications of Deans of Students and Civic Education Teachers (hereinafter referred to as the "Examination Committee") shall be separately determined.

Article 2 The term "dean of students and civic education teacher" as used in these regulations refers to a person who is currently serving or wishes to serve as a dean of students or director of instruction and a teacher of civic education courses as stipulated in the regulations for secondary schools.

Article 3 All deans of students, directors of instruction, and civic education teachers in secondary schools nationwide shall be subject to examination by the Examination Committee. Those who have not been examined or have been examined but found unqualified three months after the Examination Committee in each locality begins its work shall not continue to serve.

Article 4 All deans of students, directors of instruction, and civic education teachers in secondary schools nationwide must apply to the Examination Committee for examination themselves.

Article 5 Any member of this Party (including probationary members) or any person who has not yet joined the Party but has studied the Three Principles of the People and meets the following qualifications may apply for examination of qualifications as a dean of students or civic education teacher in secondary schools. (A) A person who has the qualifications for a secondary school teacher as stipulated by the education administrative agency and has served in a student affairs position in a secondary school may apply for examination of qualifications as a dean of students in a secondary school. (B) A person who has one of the following qualifications may apply for examination of qualifications as a civic education teacher in a secondary school: 1. A graduate of a specialized school or above who has studied social sciences and has teaching experience or has passed a test examination. 2. A person who has the qualifications for a secondary school teacher as stipulated by the education administrative agency and has taught social sciences. 3. A person who has the qualifications for a secondary school teacher as stipulated by the education administrative agency and has a solid understanding of social sciences and has written works on the subject.

Article 6 Anyone requesting examination must submit the various documents proving qualifications as stipulated in Article 5 of these regulations, as well as the following documents: Two recent half-length photographs of themselves, application form, curriculum vitae.

Article 7 Any member of this Party who meets the following qualifications may be exempt from examination, but must submit documents proving their qualifications to the Examination Committee in each locality for registration. After registration, they shall obtain the qualifications of a dean of students or civic education teacher in a secondary school: 1. Having obtained a certificate of qualification as a dean of students and a Party principles teacher, and being a graduate of a senior high school or above, and having more than two years of experience in student affairs work and teaching in a secondary school. 2. Having served as a certified Party principles teacher or a member of the committee for examining the qualifications of Party principles teachers, and being a graduate of a senior high school or above, and having more than two years of experience in student affairs work and teaching in a secondary school. 3. Currently serving or having served as a member of the Committee for the Examination of Qualifications of Deans of Students and Civic Education Teachers.

Article 8 All deans of students and civic education teachers who have passed the examination and have the qualifications stipulated in Article 7 of these regulations shall be issued a certificate of qualification by the Examination Committee.

Article 9 In localities where there is a shortage of personnel with the qualifications stipulated in Articles 5 and 7 of these regulations, the principals of the schools may propose to hire someone who has a firm understanding and belief in Party principles, has a solid understanding and experience in student affairs and civic education, and has the qualifications of a secondary school teacher as stipulated by the education administrative agency. They shall state their reasons to the Examination Committee in each locality, and after approval, they may serve as a substitute dean of students or civic education teacher.

Article 10 Before hiring a substitute dean of students or civic education teacher, each secondary school must submit the applicant's application form, curriculum vitae, school graduation certificate, documents proving their teacher qualifications, and two recent half-length photographs. If they have written works, they must also submit the works. After passing the examination and being issued a substitute certificate, they may be hired.

Article 11 Any non-Party member who has passed the examination and is a qualified dean of students or civic education teacher or a substitute may be introduced by the Examination Committee to two members of the Provincial or Special Party Headquarters Committee to become a probationary member of this Party.

Article 12 Any dean of students or civic education teacher or substitute who has passed the examination and has been hired by a school must report their work situation to the Examination Committee at least once every semester for evaluation.

Article 13 If there are any matters not covered in these regulations, the Central Ministry of People's Training may submit them to the Central Executive Committee for amendment. Article 14 These regulations shall be implemented upon resolution by the Central Executive Committee.

Revised Organizational Regulations for the Committee for the Examination of Qualifications of Deans of Students and Civic Education Teachers 148

(Passed by the Sixth Meeting of the Fifth Central Standing Committee on February 20, 1936)

Article 1 These regulations are formulated in accordance with the provisions of Article 1 of the Regulations for the Examination of Qualifications of Deans of Students and Civic Education Teachers in Secondary Schools.

Article 2 Each province or city (city directly under the Executive Yuan) may establish a Committee for the Examination of Qualifications of Deans of Students and Civic Education Teachers (hereinafter referred to as the "Examination Committee"). The number of members of the committee shall be five to seven. In addition to one member mutually recommended by the members of the Party Headquarters of each province or special city and one chief education administrator who shall be ex officio members, the remaining members shall be selected and appointed by the Party Headquarters of each province or special city in conjunction with the local education administrative agency from among Party members who are graduates of specialized schools or above and have rich educational experience. The selections shall be reported to the Central Ministry of People's Training and the Ministry of Education for record.

Article 3 The Examination Committee of each province or city (city directly under the Executive Yuan) shall be responsible for examining the qualifications of deans of students and civic education teachers in the following levels of schools: Secondary schools established by the province or city (city directly under the Executive Yuan) or by the county, and private secondary schools approved for establishment. Secondary schools attached to universities or higher specialized schools in the province or city.

Article 4 In areas where there is no Party headquarters, the highest local education administrative agency shall formulate measures based on the circumstances and submit them to the Central Ministry of People's Training for implementation.

Article 5 The Examination Committee is a permanent agency, and its members serve on a voluntary basis. The staff who assist in handling examination affairs shall be concurrently held by staff of the Party Headquarters of the province or city (city directly under the Executive Yuan) and its highest education administrative agency.

Article 6 If there are any matters not covered in these regulations, the Central Ministry of People's Training may submit them to the Central Executive Committee for amendment.

Article 7 These regulations shall be implemented upon resolution by the Central Executive Committee.

Art Teachers of Primary and Secondary Schools in This City Discussed Restoring Art Teaching Hours Yesterday 151

Over a Hundred People Attended and Immediately Established a Promotion Association

The China Art Education Society Telegraphed the Ministry of Education Yesterday Requesting Maintenance

The China Art Education Society believes that the Ministry of Education's recent revision of the curriculum standards for primary and secondary schools, which reduces the number of teaching hours for art subjects, hinders the progress of art education. Yesterday, it specially convened art teachers from primary and secondary schools throughout the city at the China Art and Learning Society for a tea party. It was unanimously resolved to telegraph the Ministry of Education to restore the original number of hours, and a promotion association was immediately established. The details are recorded below:

Participating Teachers

In addition to Shi Chongpeng, Ma Gongyu, and Wu Kechang, the executive directors of the Art Education Society, those who attended yesterday included teachers from Provincial Shanghai High School, Jingye Middle School, Xinlu Normal School, YMCA Middle School, Fudan Middle School, Wuben Girls' High School, Xinhua Art School, Shanghai Art College, Minsheng Girls' School, the First Chinese Primary School of the French Municipal Council, Minguang Middle School, Sanyu Middle School, Kaiming Middle School, Mingde Girls' High School, Shanghai High School Experimental Primary School, New Asia Middle School, and private art teachers from upper and middle schools such as Zhu Yunsong, Zhao Weizu, Chuan Boliang, Zhou Xibao, Zhu Zhiwei, Zhang Meisun, Ke Ding, Chen Yishi, He Mingzhai, Jiang Danshu, Xie Gongzhan, Yu Jifan, Chen Yuefeng, Wang Yungong, Pan Gongwang, Shen Muqu, Shi Zhifu, Zhang Shitian, and Yang Weinong, totaling over a hundred people.

Important Resolutions

Chairman Ma Gongyu, recorder Shi Chongpeng. First, the chairman reported the purpose of convening the tea party, followed by reports from Wu Kechang and Shi Chongpeng. Then, discussions were held. Regarding the proposal on how to proceed with requesting the Ministry of Education to maintain the original number of teaching hours for art subjects, it was resolved: (A) To immediately establish the Shanghai Primary and Secondary School Art Subject Teaching Hour Restoration Promotion Association, and to nominate Zhao Weizu (Provincial Shanghai High School), Pan Gongwang (Xinlu Normal School), Zhou Xibao (Jingye Middle School), Shi Wenbin (Affiliated Middle School of Fudan), Ke Ding (Minguang Middle School), Zhu Zhiwei (Kaiming Middle School), Lu Yun (Minsheng Girls' School), Zhang Shitian (Mingde Girls' High School), and Shen Ge Lu (Shanghai High School Experimental Primary School), and two representatives from the China Art Education Society as members of this association. Zhao Weizu was nominated as chairman, and the first meeting was scheduled to be held at Shangwen Primary School at 4:00 PM on Monday. (B) The Promotion Association will telegraph the Ministry of Education to issue an immediate order to restore the original number of teaching hours for art subjects. (C) The Promotion Association will telegraph art teachers nationwide to unanimously respond. (D) Representatives will be sent to Beijing to petition when necessary. (E) Letters will be sent to honorary directors of the China Art Education Society, including Cai Yuanpei, Li Shizeng, Pan Gongzhan, Chen Shuren, Liu Haisu, Chen Yuanhong, and Lin Fengmian, to unanimously express and assist in restoring the number of teaching hours for art subjects. Regarding the proposal to formulate a plan for the implementation of art education during difficult times, it was resolved to hand it over to the China Art Education Society for handling. Other proposals were omitted.

Overview of the Literacy Campaign in Fujian Province 155

Fuzhou Correspondence: The literacy campaign in Fujian Province began in 1932 and has been going on for three years with considerable success. The process can be divided into three periods: initiation, promotion, and compulsion. A detailed description follows:

Initiation Period

The implementation of literacy education in Fujian Province actually started in 1929. Due to lack of funding, not many schools were established. In 1932, Zheng Zhenwen, Director of the Department of Education, returned to Fujian to preside over educational administration. Recognizing the need to intensify literacy education, he proposed to the provincial government to organize a Popular Literacy Education Committee to handle literacy education affairs specifically. It was jointly organized by social education organizations and social groups in the provincial capital and directly under the provincial government. At the beginning of the program, publicity work was carried out first, followed by a survey of illiteracy in the city. At the same time, the Literacy Association established public schools, totaling ninety-four schools with one hundred and seventy-seven classes. Classrooms of public and private schools and public institutions were used as teaching venues, and illiterate people were notified to attend school. A total of 5,668 people enrolled in these schools. As for the teaching staff, they were filled by civil servants from various agencies and teachers from various schools, all on a voluntary basis, without subsidies. The first phase was from April to August, and a graduation test was held. As a result, 2,503 people graduated. The second phase of public schools started in September. School establishment plans gradually shifted from cities to the surrounding rural areas. Five central public schools were established in the five police districts of the provincial capital, each responsible for the administrative matters of their respective districts. A total of 110 classes were established, with over 4,500 students enrolled. Unfortunately, only two months after the start of classes, the Fujian Incident occurred, and all schools were suspended. The Literacy Association was also affected and suspended operations. This was the first phase of the literacy campaign in Fujian Province.

Promotion Period

In January 1934, the Fujian Incident was quelled. Zheng Zhenwen, Director of the Department of Education of the newly established provincial government, resumed his post, and the Popular Literacy Association was also restored on February 22. The name was changed to the Fujian Provincial Popular Literacy Committee, under the Department of Education, with a committee of seven members. In addition to the Director of the Department of Education serving as the chairman, the remaining members were appointed by the Department of Education. Immediately, the second phase of public schools continued, but after a survey, only sixty-one schools were deemed capable of opening classes, with over 1,800 students. By the time of the graduation test, 1,623 students had passed. The third phase of public schools was extended to the thirteen autonomous districts under the jurisdiction of Minhou County. A total of ninety-seven schools were established throughout the county, with some schools running two levels. In total, there were one hundred and nine classes. The teaching staff was generally appointed by the Literacy Association and started classes in March. A total of 4,940 students enrolled. By the end of July, after the test, 3,487 students graduated. The fourth phase of public schools began in September 1934. In addition to continuing to establish schools in Minhou County, the program was also extended to Changle and Jian'ou Counties. At the same time, considering that Minhou County had already run three phases of public schools and had many graduates, higher-level public schools were selectively established in villages where schools had previously been established, so that the public could have opportunities for further education. A total of five senior public schools, four central public schools, and forty-six ordinary public schools were established in Minhou County, totaling sixty-nine schools. Three central public schools and twenty-two ordinary public schools were established in Changle County, totaling thirty-three classes. Ten ordinary public schools were established in Jian'ou County, totaling ten classes. In total, ninety-two schools were established, totaling one hundred and twelve classes. The number of students was 3,427 in Minhou County, 1,618 in Changle County, and 437 in Jian'ou County, totaling 5,482. The program was completed in January 1935. The number of graduates was 2,302 in Minhou County, 1,012 in Changle County, and 257 in Jian'ou County, totaling 3,571. The fifth phase of public schools began in March 1935 and was further extended to Fuqing and Lianjiang Counties. Only senior classes and children's classes were held in Minhou County. The establishment of public schools in Jian'ou County was temporarily suspended. Schools were still established in Changle County. A total of eleven schools were established in Minhou County, running eighteen classes, with 844 students. Sixteen schools were established in Changle, running thirty-five classes, with 1,732 students. Seventeen schools were established in Fuqing County, running twenty-two classes, with 1,003 students. Nine schools were established in Lianjiang County, running thirteen classes, with 639 students. In total, fifty-three schools were established in various counties, running eighty-eight classes, with a total of 4,218 students. In July 1935, a graduation test was held, and the program was reported as completed. The total number of graduates was 611 in Minhou County, 1,162 in Changle County, 819 in Fuqing County, and 570 in Lianjiang County, totaling 3,162. The establishment of schools by the Popular Literacy Association came to an end at this point. Later, the association was ordered to carry out compulsory literacy work, entering another stage. According to statistics, the association ran five phases of public schools, establishing a total of 446 schools, with 596 classes and 19,346 graduates.

Compulsory Period

Since this method had no precedent, it could be promoted. To ensure smooth implementation, it should be tested first, to serve as a future standard for implementation. The Literacy Association began implementing compulsory literacy throughout the province last August and has been doing so for six months. Thirteen villages in the third district of Minhou and the fourth district of Changle were designated as pilot areas, and personnel were dispatched to handle them separately. Except for the third district of Minhou, which has already ended, with 4,126 people receiving compulsory literacy, the pilot area in Changle is still ongoing. As for the counties and cities in this province that have been ordered to implement compulsory literacy, they have all actively promoted it. As of the end of January 1936, a total of thirty-eight counties and cities and one special zone had established schools to implement compulsory literacy, running 1,681 schools. Excluding the 461 schools that did not report the number of students enrolled, it is known that over 56,000 people are enrolled. Seventeen counties and one special zone are also preparing to open classes by the end of February. Only eight counties and one special zone have not yet established public schools.

Mr. Huang Pinjia of this city has specially organized a Public Education Group. Scholars only need to have five or more people. The required subjects, times, and locations can be communicated to the group by letter, and teachers will be dispatched to teach in accordance with the agreement. Lectures are prepared for each subject. The group's address is No. 24, Yuehua Fang, Jingzhou Road, Huade Road.

Women's Education Center to Hold Regular Motherhood Education Competition 156

And Plans to Organize a Mothers' Association

The Shanghai Women's Education Center on Hualong Road in this city is now promoting the sense of responsibility of mothers in various families and creating a social atmosphere that values virtuous mothers. It is specially scheduled to hold a Motherhood Education Competition on Children's Day, April 4th. Any mother with children can participate. After the competition, a Mothers' Association will be organized to study the way of motherhood. The competition rules are recorded below: (1) Purpose of the competition: This center aims to promote the sense of responsibility of mothers in various families and create a social atmosphere that values virtuous mothers. A Motherhood Education Competition will be held annually on Children's Day. (2) Eligibility: Any resident of this city with a child (regardless of gender) aged five to ten can register to participate. (3) Registration procedures: Those who wish to participate should bring their children of eligible age to the center to register and submit two 4.5-inch half-length photos of the mother and child. They will receive a competition certificate and come to the center at the scheduled date and time for the competition. (4) Registration period: From March 21st to March 31st. (5) Competition date: Children's Day, April 4th, starting at 9:00 AM. If the number of participants is too large, it may be extended by one day. (6) Competition items: 1. Physical fitness, 2. Cleanliness, 3. Courtesy, 4. Response. (7) Competition order: Determined by drawing lots. Those who arrive after the specified time will be disqualified. If the number of participants is too large, the competition may be divided into groups according to age. (8) Scoring method: Total score is 100%. Physical fitness is worth 30 points, cleanliness is worth 20 points, and courtesy and response are worth 25 points. (9) Awards: 1. Those with a total score of 90 points or more will be awarded a souvenir for the mother and a toy or reading material and candy for the child. 2. Those with a total score of 80 points or more will be awarded a souvenir for the mother and a toy or reading material for the child. 3. Those with a total score of 70 points or more will be awarded a souvenir for the mother and candy for the child. 4. No awards will be given to those with less than 70 points. (10) Award date: April 6th, 10:00 AM. (11) Judges: Educational experts and well-known doctors will be hired by this center. (12) Supplementary rules: These rules will be implemented after being approved by the center's administrative meeting.

Publication of "Cultural Construction," Volume 3, Issue 6 160

China in times of crisis faces two major problems: one is the direction of national defense economic policy, and the other is the cultivation of youth. The recently published "Cultural Construction," Volume 2, Issue 6, focuses on discussing these two problems. Regarding the former, there are papers by Professors Liu Zhendong and Zheng Shubu. Regarding the latter, there are five essays, all of which study these problems from a theoretical perspective. In addition, there are many essays on land and rural issues, such as Weng Zhizhen's "An Evaluation of the Problem of Village Ownership of Land," Zhang Jueren's "On the Reform of the Old Land System in China," Chen Yun's "Disaster Relief Policy and Public Granary System," Cheng Zhicheng's "An Analysis of the Inherent Organization of Chinese Rural Society and Its Evaluation," and Ji Hongfa's "The Reality of Debt Among Chinese Farmers." Organizing farmers and consolidating the rural economy is the primary task in building our national defense economy, so the publication of these essays in this issue also has special significance. It is reported that in view of the increasingly urgent international situation, the next issue of the journal will be a "Special Issue on International Political Economy," which will feature specially commissioned articles by experts on recent major international issues, such as the world panic, tariff policy, world trade, currency issues, silver issues, the Soviet Union's Five-Year Plan, the Sino-Japanese problem, the Italian-Ethiopian problem, the disarmament problem, and the re-division of colonies. It is hoped that this journal will provide readers with valuable reading and reference materials. In addition, the journal's monthly essay contest for April is themed "A Tragic History," which requires writers to extract the most tragic and moving episodes from historical facts in this country, and describe them in a way that is relevant to the present era. The length of the article should be two to three thousand words, and the deadline is March 25th.

Children's Educational Novel

Little Men (1)(9)(8) 168

— Original by Louisa M. Alcott, translated by Zheng Xiaocang

It was only now that the greatest brilliance of the entire play was discovered. First, a thick rope was seen slapping on the stage, then suddenly it tightened and jerked, and Amy's voice was heard shouting, "Lift up, move forward!" Then the gruff voice of the Quartermaster Rice answered, "Steady—steady!" Followed by a burst of laughter, as four large gray mice appeared, their legs trembling, their tails rather peculiar, but their heads very dignified, their black whiskers looking lifelike. They: dragged—or were meant to look as if they were dragging—a tall, beautiful carriage, made from one half of that pumpkin king, placed on the wheels of Tandy's cart, the wheels being painted yellow to match the brightly colored carriage body. In the front seat was a happy little coachman, wearing a white wig, a towering hat, and red breeches and a lace-trimmed coat, whipping a long whip, tugging on several red reins, so vigorously that the four gray steeds stood up like people. This coachman was Tandy himself, he nodded and smiled at the guests, looking so funny that they gave him a round of applause; Aunt Laurie said, "If I could find such a serious coachman, I would hire him immediately." The carriage stopped, and the stepmother carried the little maiden up, and she sat high up, booming away, waving to the audience along the way, her glass slippers rising in front, and her scarlet skirt sweeping the ground behind her, because although the carriage was beautiful, the beauty sitting in it was already very cramped.

The next scene was a dance party, where Nan and May were dressed as splendidly as peacocks. Nan, playing the proud stepsister, was particularly well suited, and as she swept across the palace hall, she seemed to be able to overwhelm all the other beauties there. The prince, sitting alone on an unstable throne, gazed around from beneath a heavy crown, while twirling his sword or admiring the silk roses on his shoes. When he saw Cinderella enter, he jumped up and exclaimed in a rush, but also very warmly.

Finance: Daily Transactions Slightly Clogged, Foreign Exchange Briefly Loosened Mid-Course, Resulting in Stability 169

The exchange market yesterday was slightly clogged during the day, briefly loosened mid-course, with few transactions, resulting in a generally stable outcome. In the early morning, the telegrams indicated that London's large bars were up 0.0625 for both near and far terms. It was said that after closing, there were buyers willing to add 0.0625 to the listed price, and sellers were supposedly reluctant to sell. The New York silver market was unchanged. The forward silver price in Montreux remained unchanged. The price of London raw gold was up by half a penny. The British pound depreciated against the US dollar by 0.0375 and against the French franc by 3 pounds. The US dollar depreciated against the British pound by 0.0625 and against the French franc by 0.01. The exchange market opened in the morning with the near-term selling price of the British pound at 1 shilling 2.4375 and a half pence, and the US dollar at 30.0625 yuan, compared to the previous close, the US dollar was stable while the British pound was up by 0.03125. After opening, the near-term trend loosened slightly due to daily trading. The exchange rates announced by HSBC were unchanged for both British and US dollars. The overall trend remained stable, but limited transactions meant that there was little change in the process thereafter. The trend loosened further at noon, due to a lack of counterparties. Later, as the market stabilized slightly, banks engaged in slight swaps. The initial report on Indian silver showed an increase of 5 annas, with little change. Finally, the Indian silver price increased by another anna, but due to even more sluggish transactions, no changes occurred until closing. At closing, the near-term selling price of the British pound was 1 shilling 2.5 pence, and the US dollar was 30.0625 yuan, compared to the previous close, both British and US dollars were stable, as were the forward rates. Transactions were sparse throughout the day. While foreign firms settled in US dollars, daily traders made slight sales, and Chinese merchants remained on the sidelines. A record of the day's market conditions is provided below:

The British pound opened in the morning with the near-term selling price at 1 shilling 2.4375 and a half pence. Mitsubishi sold 4375 for April to McGarry, and Lever Bros. did the same at the same price for the same month, while Cell sold 3125 for June. At noon, the near-term selling price was 1 shilling 2.5 pence. There were few counterparties in the afternoon market. At closing, the spot price was 1 shilling 2.5 pence, 4375 and a half pence for March, 375 and 4375 for April, 3125 and 375 for May, and 25 and 3125 for June. The buying price was 0.0625 higher.

The US dollar opened in the morning with the near-term selling price at 30.0625 yuan. Mitsubishi sold 0625 for March, Mitsui McGarry sold spot 0625 to the foreign firm sector. At noon, the near-term selling price was 30.125 yuan. In the afternoon market, McGarry sold 0625 for March and bought spot 0625 and 125. Cell also sold 30 yuan for March. At closing, the selling price was 30.0625 yuan for spot, 30 yuan for March, 29.875 yuan for April, 75 yuan for May, and 625 yuan for June. The buying price was 0.0625 higher.

Yesterday, the French dollar was bought from North China for 470 francs for May.

Yarn and Cotton: Spot Goods are Tight, Yarn Market Rebounds After Attempting to Fall 173

The yarn market fell ten times in the morning. After a large increase the previous day, profit-takers started selling. At the same time, third-grade yarn fell back six or seven dimes. As a result, market sentiment slightly loosened, and the market situation slightly weakened. However, cash was extremely tight, and the financial sector absorbed at low prices. The yarn stock in Shanghai warehouses shrank, decreasing by more than 10,000 bales compared to last month. The cotton yarn itself can be considered consolidated.

Yarn is still perceived as tight this month.

The opening price of the marked yarn market in the morning was lower because the longs from the previous day released, and the situation turned loose. The Osaka third-grade yarn telegram showed a small decrease of a few dimes. The market price fell, but the situation in the current month is urgent because of the lack of spot yarn and the gradual increase in selling prices. Raw materials are expensive, and factories find it difficult to sell short. As a result, the market outlook is tighter, and shorts for distant months are still unwilling to cover and have slightly turned to fatigue. As a result, prices for each month fell by six, eight, nine dimes to one dollar and one dime compared to the closing price of the previous day. The afternoon opening market situation was still flat and weak. It was heard that spot yarn transactions were still good in the second and third sessions. The Osaka third-grade yarn result was only down six or seven dimes compared to the previous day. Cotton Inventory is Dwindling 174

Without Large Imports of Foreign Cotton, Market Prices are Not Expected to Fall

After rising sharply, cotton has returned to level. Some longs have taken profits, and the market is selling off due to loosening chips. However, the condition of spot cotton is exceptionally tight, and inventory is dwindling. Unless large quantities of foreign cotton are imported, the future of the cotton market cannot be seen as bearish.

The market opening for marked cotton saw all months fall by one or two dimes. American cotton continued to rise by six to nine points, Indian cotton was suspended, and Osaka third-grade cotton rose and fell by two or three dimes. Yuanchangxing, on behalf of a large firm from Jun, sold 15,000 dan, causing the market to sell off due to abundant chips. However, Tongji continued to buy. As a result, all months fell by two or three dimes compared to the closing price of the previous day. The afternoon opening was flat, and the second and third sessions were slightly soft. By the closing, it was heard that spot cotton consumption was active, and the market turned firm. As a result, all months rose by five fen compared to the morning closing price. Metals: Smoked Sheet Iron Prices Soar 182

Recently, smoked sheet iron has been scarce due to thin arrivals and stock, and the market atmosphere has been very good. Customer groups and enamel factories, thermos bottle factories, etc., in this street have been adding to their purchases, so there have been quite a few transactions. Prices have soared, with each dan opening as high as nine yuan, a sharp increase of three or four dimes compared to the previous day. Transactions amounted to 600 or 700 dan. In addition, the price of 3.6-foot goods has remained the same because there are not many buyers and the stock in the market is thick.

Piece Goods: Mercerized Feather Yarn Supply and Demand are Both Strong, The Result of Domestic Factory Competition 183

Domestic mercerized feather yarn is selling twice as well with the arrival of spring. Various Western clothing tailoring groups have made large purchases. The #3 and #4 goods are selling extensively. However, the selling price is cheap. The cost of silk yarn raw materials used to weave this product has increased sharply, and there is no reason for it to fall. The reason for this is that there are too many small-scale machine households at sea, causing the products to be overstocked. Because they are smaller in scale, financial resources are often insufficient, so they all adopt a low-profit principle in order to compete for sales. This makes the market more and more fatigued. The group patterned mercerized feather yarn are all selling at four dimes, and fine patterned are four dimes and three fen.

Yuanfang Auction House Sales are Not Smooth 184

German's Inspection of Sino-German Trade Talks 186

Shanghai Dispatch from the National Maritime News Agency, March 11: Dr. Klepp, head of the German Far East Economic Investigation Group, gave a speech at the Pan-Pacific Association in this city today on "The German Economic Situation." One section on Sino-German trade stated: "Although Germany is under import restrictions, it still imports large quantities of raw materials to meet the needs of industry, so that the unity and planning under the new economic policy can be realized. Due to the lack of foreign exchange, Germany's payment for raw materials purchased abroad relies solely on the export of industrial products to those countries. This is the reason why Germany's imports from certain countries are less or more than from other countries. Under this system, according to a report by the China Social and Economic Research Institute, the import of Chinese products to Germany increased by 45% from 1934 to 1935. We believe that the upward trend is still likely to continue. Currently, assuming that the production of raw materials in various countries around the world will always increase without end, and that Germany's export of industrial products is also sufficient to offset the import price of raw materials, the premise for implementing Germany's economic system can also be considered resolved."

Finance in the Past Year (Continued 4) 188

— He Boxiong

Generally speaking, from January to May of last year, all exchange rates consistently rose. In June and July, the exchange market experienced a decline, starting with foreign banks and spreading downwards. The British exchange rate fell from 1 shilling 7 and 125/10000 pence to 1 shilling 6 and 75/100 pence, and the US exchange rate fell from 39.3125 US dollars to 36.75 US dollars. Around early August, there was a slight increase in trade exports and sluggishness in imports. Logically, there should have been changes in foreign exchange rates. However, for several months, the actual commercial exchange needs accounted for very little. The reason for this was that people were generally cautious about the future. Therefore, when London silver prices fell in mid-August, Shanghai exchange rates moved in the opposite direction, which was clearly due to the manipulation of powerful speculators. Since the implementation of the equalization tax in October of last year, the exchange rate has become detached from parity. Its fluctuations can be artificially controlled, and it only stabilized towards the end of the month. The exchange market was uneventful in September. In October, the key factor that could cause changes in exchange rates was the future of China's currency problem. Rumors of currency inflation and devaluation had been circulating for a long time, and were particularly intense in that month. The exchange rate of Shanghai against foreign currencies declined steadily amidst these rumors. The British exchange rate even decreased from 1 shilling 6 and 8125/10000 pence on October 1st to 1 shilling 2 and 75/100 pence on the 31st. The two-month forward price of the British exchange rate reached a low of 1 shilling 2 and 625/10000 pence. The US exchange rate fell from 38 and a half dollars to 30 and 3125/10000 dollars. The differences between the exchange rates before and after were more than 4 pence for the British exchange rate and more than 8 dollars for the US exchange rate. In early November, the British exchange rate decreased by half a penny per national currency unit, and the US exchange rate decreased by one US dollar per hundred national currency units. This was due to the Ministry of Finance's announcement on the 4th to cease the use of silver currency and ordering the three banks to buy and sell foreign exchange without restrictions. Article 6 of the Ministry of Finance's emergency decree stated: "In order to stabilize the exchange rate of legal tender against foreign currencies at the current price, the Central Bank, the Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications shall buy and sell foreign exchange without restrictions" (Note 6). Therefore, from November 4th, the posted prices of the Central Bank, which are the official rates, were fixed at 1 shilling 2 pence for 1 yuan of legal tender for the British exchange rate, 29 and three-quarters US dollars for 100 yuan of legal tender for the US exchange rate, and 103 yuan of Japanese currency for 100 yuan of legal tender, without any changes. The following is a table summarizing the fluctuations of various exchange rates over the past year: (Note 7)
