Gold Bar Market

The Shanghai Gold Bar Market sometimes has the power to influence the exchange market and finance. The changes in the gold market are often dramatic, especially in February and April. The following table shows the fluctuations in the gold market over the past year: (Note 8)

Shanghai Gold Bar Market Prices in the Republic of China Year 24

Month Highest Lowest Difference

January 976.5 942.0 34.5

February 978.7 872.0 106.5

March 897.5 806.0 91.5

April 897.5 741.5 158.0

May 801.7 749.8 51.9

June 839.0 746.1 92.9

July 908.0 821.0 87.0

August 918.8 863.2 55.6

September 900.2 856.3 39.4

October 1217.0 879.2 237.8

November 1183.0 1106.0 77.0

In January of last year, the gold market was extremely quiet. In February, gold prices steadily declined with very few rebounds. The highest price for the entire month was 978.7 yuan, and the lowest was 872 yuan. The difference in January reached a significant 106.5 yuan. The reasons for this sharp decline are: The US gold bar scheme was adjudicated, and the government largely won. The Ministry of Finance repeatedly encouraged silver imports. Rumors circulated that a Sino-British loan was about to be established. Overseas silver prices steadily increased. As a result, market prices fell below the 900 yuan mark. In March, the downward trend in gold prices continued unabated. One reason was that countries using gold deliberately manipulated methods to lower the value of their currencies. Another reason was that China's outflow of silver currency was too large, forcing it to purchase silver in London and sell gold bars in Shanghai. As a result, the gold market plunged sharply, only to stabilize in the middle of the month. In the last ten days of the month, Sassoon, a British merchant, suggested issuing Shanghai pound bonds with British loans, and the US banker Thomas's silver amendment was rejected by the House of Representatives. In addition, there was a shortage of chips in the gold market, creating a short squeeze situation. Gold prices rose sharply, approaching the 890 yuan mark. In April, a reaction occurred again, and gold prices fell again. The daily difference also increased from more than 10 yuan to more than 30 yuan. On the 25th, rumors spread that the US government officially raised silver prices, and the downward trend became even more severe, with a sharp drop of 30 yuan in one day. The lowest price in the gold market for that month was 741.5 yuan, which was the first new low since the settlement price of customs gold in the previous year. In May, the market situation showed a revolving trend. The highest gold price was the closing price of 801.7 yuan on the 8th, and the lowest price was 749.8 yuan on the 18th. Throughout the month, gold prices fluctuated between 750 yuan and 800 yuan. In June, it hovered around 770 yuan. In the last ten days of the month, the market situation suddenly turned upward, breaking through the 800 yuan mark on the 22nd. This was due to the Central Bank's shipment of gold for export and rumors of currency inflation. In July, August, and September, there were no special changes in gold prices. In October, the gold exchange experienced a frenzy unprecedented in its history, rising from 879.2 yuan to 1211 yuan, a difference of 337.8 yuan. Although the Central Bank tried its best to maintain it, it was difficult to reverse the wild surge. In the last few days of the month, rumors spread that China's currency reform would be implemented in early November, and there was talk that the customs gold unit would soon be raised to 2 yuan 5. Large investors bought aggressively, and retail investors followed suit, pushing gold prices straight into the sky, reaching a new high of 1210 yuan on the 31st. In November, the events had already been implemented, and the gold market also lost its heroic posture (to be continued)

Shen Bao Literary Weekly

A Person Seeking Sympathy 189

— Lin Shi

Professor Lu felt that he had rarely been so melancholic in recent years, and today he seemed to be experiencing the deepest taste of melancholy. He really couldn't stay in the house, he had to go for a walk outside no matter what. Moreover, he was a man without a family, and there was no woman to comfort him, so he felt particularly empty from morning to night. This emptiness could not be filled no matter how hard he paced back and forth, blowing smoke rings. The only opportunity was when the servant brought tea, and he really wanted to talk to him, but as soon as he saw his usual reserved and dull appearance, he simply couldn't talk to him for more than half a sentence, so he could only stare at him as he added some coal to the stove, and then stare at him as he silently, like a ghost, moved his two feet straight out of the room. And even the bit of vitality that he had just brought in was still taken away, leaving only the slight cracking sound of the coal in the stove. This made Professor Lu turn from melancholy to anger, and he angrily threw the half-smoked cigarette on the ground and stomped it out, as if smoking was what was making him annoyed. He immediately and nimbly put on his overcoat and prepared to go out. But turning around, he saw the cigarette butt he had just extinguished, which would inevitably dirty the floor, and it was a pity to waste most of the cigarette, so he calmly picked it up and put it on the table, then straightened his back and walked out the door.

Coming out of the door, he still felt melancholic, and it seemed that the streetlights were also much dimmer tonight. The north wind blew hard on his face, and he had to shrink his head into the collar of his cloak.

He walked a long way and turned many corners, but he had not yet decided where to go. Soon, a Beijing opera theater was nearby, so he bought a seat and went into the theater. Sure enough, it was very lively inside, and the atmosphere was very different from outside. Just the joyful expressions of the audience and the smoke were enough to warm up the place. But before long, he regretted coming in. There were many reasons: for example, the drums and cymbals on the stage were so noisy that they almost pierced his eardrums. Usually, he always felt that he could relax in the theater, but today he hated that the musicians were deliberately making trouble for him. And the audience members coughed incessantly, their foreheads and necks strained. They used various postures and sounds to compete to spit phlegm, spitting here and spitting there, as if they had originally agreed to spend money to come here to spit phlegm, otherwise it would not be worth spending money for nothing. This made Professor Lu sigh several times, indicating that he was really annoyed. There were also many women who were desperately cracking melon seeds, enjoying the jokes of the clowns on stage, not understanding Professor Lu's melancholy mood at all, which also made him very angry. In short, the people here were indifferent to Professor Lu, no one comforted him, no one paid attention to him, as if he did not exist in the world at all, but he thought this was very wrong. Of course, he was also quite able to sympathize with himself, and he wanted to say to the people next to him:

"Hey! Today I read the foreign newspapers in Shanghai, and my brother was beaten to death, that's right. You know he was very young, and he really shouldn't have died." But would the listener sympathize with him? No, he guessed right; besides, everyone sitting there was someone he didn't know.

He angrily walked out of the theater, because he believed that he would definitely not find any comfort here. The only way was to talk to Mr. Zhou, who he usually associated with most closely. He walked west, not forgetting that Mr. Zhou lived in a hutong on the edge of the department.

The wind was still blowing, but at least it wasn't raining.

Along the way, Professor Lu felt more and more sad; his brother's bloody head was vaguely in front of him. Thinking of this, he almost cried.

When he arrived at Mr. Zhou's study, Mr. Zhou was busy writing at his desk, and casually let him sit down next to him. Because there was a fire in the room, he took off his overcoat and sat down, without saying a word. Afterwards, Mr. Zhou put down his pen, turned around and said to him:

"These days, while the students are on strike, I want to finish my political theory. I've already written three-fifths of it. But I'm busy writing all day long, and my hands hurt."

Professor Lu didn't answer a word, just listened. Then Mr. Zhou said again:

"What's wrong with you? How do you spend your time these days? While school is not in session, you don't write anything, and staying in the house is also boring."

"Hmm!"

"Yesterday I played cards once," Mr. Zhou said again, "My luck wasn't bad, I won twenty-some dollars."

"Hmm." Professor Lu was always "hmm," which disappointed Mr. Zhou, and he turned around again to write his lecture notes, it seemed that he had to finish writing them tonight. Leaving Professor Lu staring blankly at the fire in the stove. Because he was too close to the stove, his legs were burned painfully. This made him think of the stove at home, and when he left, he forgot to tell the servant to turn it off. Burning until now, it must have been a waste. He thought he had to go home, but he was determined to come and talk to Mr. Zhou, how could he run back without saying a word? He lit a cigarette, and after smoking for a long time, Mr. Zhou was still busy writing his lecture notes and ignoring him. Looking at his watch, it was almost half past ten, and he finally spoke to Mr. Zhou:

"Hey, my brother was recently beaten to death."

"Oh? Do you still have a brother?" Mr. Zhou didn't turn around, still writing non-stop.

Professor Lu decided to go home immediately, and perhaps only his servant could sympathize with him. He quickly walked onto the road home. Walking, without joy or sorrow, only a slight resentment.

This person seeking sympathy thought of his dead brother, and also thought of the unextinguished fire at home; the anger in his heart was burning.

Incense 190

— TK

Fisherman 191

— Liu Ming

— Northern Sketch Two —

The tide slowly recedes, and the sea gradually thins. Previously submerged reefs now jut out jaggedly, revealing their dark green or reddish-brown forms, like a group of sea creatures sunning their backs in the early morning light.

Sun Da-hanzi walked along the Houhai embankment, glanced at the bay, and quickly quickened his pace. The wet sand on the uneven pavement splashed up behind his heels. He usually didn't pay attention to clocks, and neither he nor his neighbors could afford such luxuries, but he could gauge the days and times by the tides that regularly rose and fell outside his door.

Walking with him was a neighbor on his way to the Dongyang Abattoir to slaughter cattle. He wore several sharp knives slung across his body with a leather belt and long rubber boots on his feet. (If his clothes weren't stained with cow blood, he would look quite like a general.) A short pipe was clamped in the corner of his mouth as he trudged along, saying that once the American naval pier on the Houhai embankment was completed, foreign soldiers would disembark here, and he'd bet everything would improve. If his friends chipped in, they could open a deli and get the rotten beef scraps and blood from the company, stew it for the rickshaw pullers serving the foreign soldiers – that would be something! Though his words were like the casual morning banter, saying whatever came to mind, ultimately, he subtly wanted to leave the company, be his own boss, and run a small business. Sun Da-hanzi wasn't interested in this. He worked for a foreign fishing company, and even if he ever dreamed, it was nothing more than returning to the days when he sailed a boat with two crewmen to Jiaozhou Bay and the farther reaches of the sea to make a living fishing. Besides, the sea's appearance and the tide's retreat were telling him it was getting late, so naturally, he wasn't in the mood to listen to his neighbor's idle talk.

"Hey, what's the rush? If you go too early, they might not even be open yet."

"What do you mean? Look over there, it's going to be late today!"

As Sun Da-hanzi hurried along, he waved toward the bay on the side of the road, signaling his neighbor to look at nature's clock.

But his neighbor, though living by the sea and close to it, was unfamiliar with the sea's nature. He casually followed Sun Da-hanzi's pointing direction, took the short pipe from his mouth, and tapped off the ashes.

Near the sea, the American naval pier had just erected many cement pillars in the water. Beside it, a small mechanical tugboat was pulling a string of iron dredgers, which looked like many turtles constantly emerging from the water.

Further away, small boats with tea-brown sails, filled with morning wind, were laden with foreign goods, taking advantage of the receding tide to sail out of the bay.

Everything was much the same as usual, and he couldn't see the significance of what Sun Da-hanzi was pointing at. But there was no need to rush and listen to him for a detailed explanation, because he had long been accustomed to it and was no longer surprised. Since pawning his boat and nets, this gloomy fisherman had taken to saying things that made no sense. Moreover, he was just chatting casually, passing the time along the way, so why bother calculating anything else?

So, seeing Sun Da-hanzi leave him behind, he immediately started talking about something else with another person nearby.

The foreign fishing company was on the edge of the small port. Several small boats called "Something-Maru" were lined up one after another in front of the door. Some short, stocky foreign fishermen, wearing dirty white towels tied around their heads and long rubber boots on their feet, were busy hauling fish and ice from the hold. Chinese coolies carried the boxes, two men per box, from the ship to the company, like a colony of ants moving house.

Everyone was extremely busy, except for a short, thin middle-aged man wearing leather riding boots, whose attitude was very relaxed. He would stand on the shore or in the aisle, holding a straight wooden stick, using it to tap the tips or sides of his riding boots.

Sun Da-hanzi ran up to him, wiping the sweat from his forehead with the fishy sleeve of his shirt, and anxiously explained that the reason he was late was that his wife and children were sick, and he had to stay home for a while. He hoped to be forgiven and not have his wages deducted.

"Oh, your wife and young master are sick," the thin, short man squinted at Sun Da-hanzi. "Why did you even come to work? You should have stayed home to take care of them." With that, he walked to the aisle by the door.

Seeing that he wasn't angry, Sun Da-hanzi didn't mind that his words didn't sound right. He walked straight in, intending to start working. But the thin, short man placed his stick across the doorway and said coldly:

"Why don't you listen? I told you to go home."

Then, he raised his voice:

"Move aside, move aside, look, you're bumping into people!"

He then quietly walked to the shore, continuing to tap the tips of his riding boots with the wooden stick.

Sun Da-hanzi followed behind him, pleading in a low voice, while thinking angrily: This three-inch runt, I could knock him into the sea with one punch. But he also understood that what threatened him by this harbor wasn't this small thing, but something bigger and more terrifying, like a demon, which he couldn't express. So he had to bend over and say pitiful things to this little thing.

The thin, short man remained cold and calm, without any sign of anger. When the giant's lowered forehead was about to touch his shoulder, he squinted and said:

"You should take a day off to rest, or else you'll get sick too, like your wife and young master."

Sun Da-hanzi could only force a bitter smile.

"Sir, don't joke around. We poor people will go hungry if we don't work for a day."

The thin, short man walked away along the shore. Sun Da-hanzi still lowered his head and followed him.

"Sir, please do a good deed. My wife and son, uh, are so sick they can't get up, they might even... (his voice choked up) let me work for one day, even if it's just half a day's wage, uh, please?"

The thin, short man's heart twitched, but he saw that there were fewer fishing boats at the dock this morning, so there was less work than usual. Why add another person? He walked away a few steps in silence, without looking at the giant beside him.

Several Koreans, wearing unclean white clothes and skirts, carrying small tin buckets, walked down the dock to call for a small boat. They were going to the island to collect oysters and seaweed, laughing and chatting lightly along the way.

The thin, short man stared at them, and even when their boat was already floating in the harbor, he hadn't looked away for a while.

Sun Da-hanzi tried his best to suppress his choked voice.

"Sir, there's not a single copper left in my house... and... and I can't borrow any... I must earn some wages today to go home and buy... buy medicine."

The thin, short man suddenly forgot himself, touched Sun Da-hanzi's waist like an old friend, and said:

"Look, which one of those bitches is pretty?"... Damn it, why don't you sit down? Huh, you must be flashing your waist."

When he finished the last two sentences, his eyes looked back at the harbor. One of the Korean women on the boat was the youngest and had a plump face. She hadn't been sitting down and was suddenly swayed by the boat twice, causing her body to lean to the side. The women on the boat burst into laughter. The laughter and the fishy sea breeze were carried together.

Sun Da-hanzi couldn't help but raise his head and look in that direction, but his eyes were a little moist, and he couldn't see anything clearly. He could only see some blurred shadows of boats coming and going on the water.

A Person Died 192

— Lin

The February spring wind howls on the sea,

The Huangpu River roars day and night,

Oh, what ominous news does it bring?

People gather in groups on street corners to discuss.

Their cheeks are red,

Their eyes burn with hatred,

A person died! A person was killed!

The spring wind carries their trembling voices.

Who is he? What is his crime?

Ah, that is none of your concern, noble sir.

He was lowly, hungry, and discontented,

His death is not worth the concern of you gentlemen,

But he had a companion,

Who suffered the same fate eleven years ago,

One you are familiar with,

Whose death once shook the world!

Yet this one died silently, unknown,

His name is not worthy to be on your lips,

Only we fools will remember him,

Forever, forever we will not forget his grievances!

The February spring wind blows across the entire earth,

The Huangpu River roars day and night,

A person died! A person was killed!

The trembling voice will reach the whole world!

A Minor Illness 193

— Wei Zhongtian

Although my body can't be said to be very good, in the past two or three years, despite going hungry many times, being frightened many times, smelling the stench of purple blood in corpses, and hearing various cries from hell, I haven't had a single illness, which is something to be thankful for amidst misfortune. I often feel comforted by this.

Unexpectedly, I recently had a minor illness. However, since it's just called an "illness," it can't be called "misfortune," can it? After all, in this day and age, illness or hunger is very common for the poor. As a joke, "illness might be beneficial to the poor, because being sick for three or five days can save three or five days' worth of food." But this only applies to a "minor illness." If it's a major illness, that won't do, because a major illness requires going to the hospital, but where will the medical expenses come from?

To be honest, if a person is idle without work and has a poor life, then a minor illness or two is indeed not a bad thing. A "minor illness," of course, doesn't require seeing a doctor or taking medicine. Quietly hiding in bed provides a better opportunity to reflect on the past and future. Past: Where and when did I get hit by the enemy's hidden arrow? When did I get bitten by a dog?… Future: When will the world change color? When will people stop eating people's blood?… Only during a minor illness, repeatedly reflecting on these things, does a different kind of feeling bury itself in the heart.

On Utopian Novels 194

— Zhiying

"Utopian novels" occupy a significant position in modern literary history. Books such as Morris's "News from Nowhere," Sinclair's "The Millennium," and Jack London's "The Iron Heel" have already been introduced to China, and there are similar works in our own country, such as Zhang Tianyi's "Ghost Earth Diary" and Lao She's "Cat Country."

As an important genre in literary phenomenon, it is worthy for us to study. We should look at the essence of utopian novels (utopian fiction) from the basic point of view of society, and then we can criticize the value of utopian novels. Moreover, we must limit the scope of discussion here, that is, the utopian novels we are talking about are social utopian novels. Things like "Journey to the West" or the Tang people's "Travels of the Immortals" are not within the scope of our discussion.

In the development history of social utopian novels, Morris of England is a typical author. Morris was born in England in the second half of the nineteenth century. In the 1860s and 1870s, British bourgeois society still preserved a lovely "stability" and flashed the brilliance of the "Golden Age." Therefore, Morris as a writer was an artistic aesthete. But in the 1880s, because of the impact of emerging bourgeois countries such as Germany and the United States, the British economy showed embarrassment. As a result, domestic class struggles were particularly obvious and sharpened. On this social economic foundation, Morris's aestheticism also changed in the beauty of his works; this is because Morris's aestheticism was not combined with pure idealist mysticism. Reality has produced tragic darkness under the deformed system, and all development and freedom have become slaves to wealth and power. Morris knew that in such an environment, art would necessarily die out, because mankind was heading towards decline. Therefore, he developed a sense of revulsion towards this system. This revulsion prompted him to devote himself to the social movement, and he wanted to use beauty and art to encourage the development of the movement of the lower classes. However, as a member of the petty bourgeoisie, he could not resolutely take off the cloak of nostalgia for the past, and he still retained his past artistic paradise fantasy. Frieche aptly described this as "the intertwining of revolutionary and archaeological studies". This "intertwining" of dissatisfaction with the present, longing for the past, and fantasizing about the future is artistically reflected in his famous novel "News from Nowhere". In this novel, the symphony of a future society of freedom and equality and a handicraft society of the fourteenth and fifteenth centuries is played, that is, the future society that appears in Morris's mind is a free paradise of agriculture and handicrafts in which machines and cities have disappeared. Needless to say, such a novel is "utopian", but it has a positive dynamic for transforming mankind.

After the World War, the social and economic situation deteriorated even further. Almost everywhere on earth was filled with the illusion of hunger and death, disease and distress. This was especially evident in Germany, which was the hardest hit. As a result, the petty-bourgeois intellectuals were burdened with heavy social despair and gave rise to a surrealistic psychology and hope. At this time, utopian novels were extremely popular. This tendency generally had a common point, that is, the fantasy that after the extinction of all mankind, a special remnant of people would recreate a beautiful paradise on earth. This is the "ideal world" of petty-bourgeois writers in the early twentieth century. Typical works of utopian novels at this time include Werner Scheff's "Stoker" in Germany, Sinclair's "The Millennium" in the United States, and Karel Čapek's "R.U.R." in Czechoslovakia.

Werner Scheff's "Stoker" is entirely a manifestation of the "despair science" of the German petty bourgeoisie after the war. This novel tells how Germany was bound by the Treaty of Versailles after the war, but the national industry and technology have achieved unprecedented development. A genius technician invented a large submarine that could pass through the water for several days and nights. At the launching of the submarine in a public ceremony, a Japanese professor predicted that the world would be destroyed immediately, but people thought he was a madman. So the submarine was launched. After a day and night, the genius technician drove the submarine back to the port, but the mechanical propeller was taken away by the Japanese professor, and the people on the boat fell into urgent despair. After many troubles, the Japanese professor returned the propeller, and the boat floated to the surface. However, all living things on earth have been poisoned by the Japanese professor's prophecy and have completely died out! The French, the authors of the Treaty of Versailles, are all dead! The people who are fortunate enough to be saved at this time thank the Japanese professor and begin to build a new life on earth.

Sinclair's "The Millennium" is set in the United States. The "philosophy" expressed in this work is roughly similar to that of Werner Scheff. He writes that a great American tycoon has a towering building, a new type of mysterious aircraft, as well as an element that can destroy all living things on earth, and a food that can satisfy the stomach for a long time with a small amount. When the element that destroys all things is activated, the tycoon and his family are sitting in the plane, so they are not destroyed. When they come back, they start to live their lives on this desolate earth. People who have always been parasites now become the builders of the world. They go from a state of primitive chaos, through the feudal era, the capitalist era, and finally reach the era of the "republic", an era where you cannot eat if you do not work.

Karel Čapek's "R.U.R." also announced the extinction of mankind at the end. At that time, the petty bourgeoisie of Czechoslovakia was threatened by the progressive movement in Hungary, and dared not accept the real reality. Therefore, this progressive movement is entirely attributed to the abyss of destruction. But in this work, the beauty of nature and the undiminished power of human nature are finally proclaimed. In short, in Čapek's works, there is also the desire to return history to the earliest state of mankind before history, and to transform the inevitable struggle of human society into a religious morality of non-resistance.

In addition, the writer who has most completely preserved the classical utopian novels is the Swedish writer Modoza, Ido Ka. He has a utopian work called "The Modern Future Novel" "The Sun's", which describes the future world divided into five countries, controlled by fifty "She Wei Yi". His ideal is the "Trinity of Body, Reason, and Essence". Future people are all "Modozaists". The so-called "Modozaists" are those who try their best to "assimilate with great undertakings" the inherent positive characteristics of mankind - strength and will. His ideal is a mixture of Wilsonian democracy and the utopia of modern urban intellectuals, and even the compromise of Gilt's small business.

Social utopian novels have slightly different expressions in new literature. We can take Jack London's "Iron Heel" as a typical utopian novel for observation.

The main difference between this new utopian novel and the tradition of previous utopian novels is that it does not eliminate social struggle. As described above, past utopian writers all used technological development and the destruction of human ethics to destroy mankind, and then rebuild a "free paradise." This thought has been completely abandoned in the utopian novels of new literature. This is most clearly expressed in Jack London's "Iron Heel". In this work, social struggle is depicted in an abstract utopian form. Jack London's "Iron Heel" is almost entirely made with new economics, that is, economics that explains and reforms the existing system, as the foundation. In form, it is almost a propagandistic paper product. The form of this work, that is, the form of semi-utopian semi-fantasy, is mainly because the author does not deeply understand reality, and his subjectivity (for example, Jack London was originally an individualist and romanticist) contradicts what he theoretically recognizes, so he cannot depict social struggle in a more concrete image; he can only depict it in an abstract utopian form.

In our country, utopian novels like the ones mentioned above have not been seen. Works such as "Ghost Earth Diary" and "Cat Country," although in form adopt utopian novels, are mainly satirical novels in content. Of course, in these works, we cannot grasp the concrete realistic understanding of art, although there are achievements in some parts. This is a utopian satirical novel related to the lineage of "Gulliver's Travels".

According to Matcha's analysis, this kind of utopian novel is not useful for new literature. Because it hides the absoluteness and immutability of human "nature".

Standing on the new world view of realism, of course, this subjective creative method should be abandoned. But if we say that this kind of utopian novel is of no use to us at all, it is too general a statement. What we abandon is mainly the utopian novelist's aspect of recognizing reality. We want to create new works with "utopian" elements, works that are consistent with the development of reality, new "utopian novels".

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Talks

Starting from the "Jewish Hotel" 195

— Xing An

As long as racial prejudice is not eradicated, conflicts between humans will be difficult to eliminate. The German exclusion of Jews is truly without limit! Since the National Socialist Party came to power in Germany, Jews residing in Germany have been repeatedly excluded. The oppression and humiliation suffered by Jews at the hands of Germans is truly unspeakable. But what can be done about it? Under violent oppression, the weak can only swallow their anger. Moreover, Jews are pitiable people who have lost their homeland!

Haven't we seen another insult now? A new hotel has recently been opened in Hanover, Germany, which is exclusively for Jews to dine in. Because since the implementation of the Nuremberg Laws, it has been extremely difficult for Jewish families to hire servants. All tasks, such as purchasing and cooking food, must be done personally, which is very inconvenient. Therefore, the authorities have this facility to make up for it. However, this hotel does not allow Aryans to enter. Germany's ban on marriage between Aryans and Jews was legally stipulated and implemented long ago. Now, Aryans are not even allowed to eat with Jews in restaurants. This kind of discriminatory treatment is the ultimate in insult!

But what can insult do? The Germans claim to be God's chosen people, the most excellent people in mankind. Jews, needless to say, are inferior. How can inferior people be equal to excellent people? Moreover, in the eyes of Germans, Jews are still the worst people in society who commit the most crimes. Previously, a German police commander made a report, saying that according to German crime statistics, the number of crimes committed by Jews was the highest. Therefore, it is only natural that Jews are despised by Germans. Furthermore, Hitler also said that Jews live in Germany as if they were eating and trampling on the land, but they are not grateful to their masters and even forget their place, committing evil and doing wrong. This is even more unforgivable!

However, are Jews the only race that suffers humiliation? In fact, it is not correct to say that this humiliation originates from racial differences. It is better to think of it as a relationship of national strength. Jews are insulted because they have lost their country. China is insulted because its international status is low. Isn't Japan also of the yellow race, but how do they treat us?

A Street Without Color 196

— Family Member

Although it is a street, it lacks the color usually associated with streets, and its appearance is unique. Specifically, it lacks modern, exquisite buildings, large department stores with lavish window displays, and vibrant advertisements fluttering in the air, which usually drape the street in a more brilliant robe. Streets adorned with these man-made creations appear exceptionally magnificent. Even the people walking on the street seem quite leisurely, strolling with a slow pace, leisurely browsing the sights.

But this street is entirely different—a street without color.

Narrow and cramped, the walkways are composed of uneven pebbles and sandy soil. When it rains, water inundates it, the soil dissolves, and the pebbles are exposed, creating potholes everywhere. The road practically turns into a mire. Whenever I have to pass through it, even if it's not a very long distance, it often takes me half a day, as I have to watch where I step and be careful not to slip and fall. By the time I cross this street, my shoes are covered in mud. I can't help but develop an unconscious aversion to it—a street to be avoided. Yet, it is a street to be avoided that I traverse daily, at least twice a day. Because of this, I have gradually become very familiar with the people who live on the street and the street's condition over time.

Almost every time I pass by, I hear women cursing men, or habitually beating children, or children fighting and crying amongst themselves in groups, all kinds of noisy sounds. If you pause to observe a bit longer, a more exciting drama often unfolds before your eyes:

Perhaps in the morning, a woman rushes out of a low wooden house onto the street, her hair unkempt, disheveled and covering her forehead, her collar unbuttoned, revealing a glimpse of her pale chest.

“Heavens, the two chickens in the coop behind my house that were laying eggs have suddenly disappeared. It must be that short-lived gambling ghost, Sanxi Zi, who stole them!”

She shouts this as she hops, and storms into Sanxi Zi’s house next door to demand the stolen chickens back.

People gather around to gossip.

If neither side admits wrongdoing, a quarrel ensues, filled with vicious curses. If it still cannot be resolved, the men of both families are drawn into the fray. What starts as a quarrel between women often ends with physical violence between men, escalating out of control before it settles.

No one saw whether Sanxi Zi really stole the chickens, and of course, there is no evidence. However, the neighbors sympathize with the victim because Sanxi Zi is indeed a bad guy, notorious on the street. Everyone despises him because he is a burly fellow who doesn't bother to find work, but instead mooches around all day, living idly and gambling like crazy. But he has no income at all, so where does the money come from? Therefore, whenever anyone loses something, even if it wasn't Sanxi Zi, people are bound to suspect that he was involved. Sanxi Zi is not the only one living licentiously on the street. Everyone looks down on such people.

In this, I occasionally discover the expression of people's most sincere emotions and the dividing line between good and evil.

Driven by life, they show no signs of fatigue—perhaps their nerves are numb. Except for a few unruly individuals, everyone expresses regret or sighs when they talk together. Everyone earnestly and bravely faces the whip of life, toiling relentlessly year after year. They live in dark, dilapidated, pigeon-coop-like wooden houses on the dirty street, perfectly content, without any other extravagant desires.

But I am always disgusted by its chaos and commotion, while they are all very accustomed to it. What is particularly annoying is that on sunny days, as you walk along, your neck is always brushed by dense bamboo poles, messily draped with newly washed, tattered clothing, including women’s shorts and children’s diapers, like an open-air art exhibition. Water drips down, possibly onto your neck, hair, or face, and you can only resent your bad luck:

A street without color!

Nonsense 197

— (Blowing)

Old Man Hu said, the Great War ended, and Germany and the other nations signed the Treaty of Versailles, but only eighteen years have passed. Now, the Great Mongol armies are once again advancing mightily, heading for the Rhine. The nations are alarmed and helpless. I think foreigners are really resourceful.

French Foreign Minister Flandin said, "If even one German soldier is stationed on the Rhine, there can be no negotiations." The German government stated, "Withdrawing troops from the Rhine is absolutely out of the question." If the German army withdraws from the Rhine, France will lose face. It’s truly a case of an unmovable object hitting an irresistible force, somewhat awkward. Now, let's see how the English, as mediators, advise.

Black Shadow 198

— Black Ding

As soon as the second Beijing-Shanghai express train has left the station, his work is done. He leaves the ticket booth and enters the luggage room, signs his name on the register, and slips out like a gray, defeated mouse. He shivers, raises the collar of his coat to his neck, and awkwardly scratches his hair with his frozen fingers. He has no desire to linger around there. He takes a deep breath of cold air. He reaches out and wipes his dry, astringent mouth, which hasn’t had a bite to eat or a drop to drink from five in the morning until one twenty in the afternoon, and feels a bitter taste lingering. Nora (9) 199

— Written by Wan Chao Chen, Explained by Xin Xin

Mrs. Lindon: (Standing up) The bell rang outside. I’d better go.

Nora: No need, just sit. No one comes here. It must be for Tao Fo.

Ailan: (At the door) Madam, there is a guest who wants to see the master.

Nora: Who is the guest?

Korek: (At the door) Mrs. Hao, it’s me.

(Mrs. Lindon is startled and quickly hides by the window.)

Nora: (Approaching Korek, sounding anxious, and speaking softly) Is that you? What’s the matter? What do you want to talk to my husband about?

Korek: Well—it’s about the bank. I have a small position at the bank, and I heard your husband has become our new manager.

Nora: So you think—

Korek: Mrs. Hao, only for some unpleasant matters, nothing else.

Nora: Then please go sit in his study.

He had been suffering from headaches for several days, and he wasn’t eating as much as usual. He was mired in melancholy and had no interest in his work. Yet, he knew this was life. Occasionally, he remembered the hunger, poverty, and unease he experienced before getting this small job, and he felt content. But when he realized that he was taking the twenty yuan he earned each month home, he would often clench the bills tightly in his hand in despair, staring angrily at the darkening ceiling for a long time without saying a word. He was thinking that he couldn't provide his wife and children with a peaceful and happy life. Gradually, his vision filled with scattered, intangible black shadows.

It had been almost three months since he joined the railway. In this bleak season, his heart was chilled by the winter air. Windy days, snowy days, rainy days, his shadow, like a ghost, mournfully walked home from the station, and from home to the station. Sometimes, late at night, when he stepped out of the station and walked home on the desolate, silent streets, or passed through dark corners, one might suspect him of being a homeless vagrant. Even more often, when he finished his work and went home at 5:30 in the morning, his eyes were blurred, and everything he saw looked like a string of interwoven red and black numbers. He just walked forward with his head down, his head buried in his coat collar. When he reached the alley, he took out his key from his pocket, opened the door, climbed the stairs, unlocked his own door, and quietly, listlessly, jumped into bed. Within minutes, he was asleep, still and peaceful like a dead man.

Today, when he just stepped into his house, he saw the one-eyed landlady was nagging his wife about something. After he asked, he found out she was asking for the rent. He didn’t use a gentle tone, and started off unreasonably and rudely: “…Could it be that we can owe you? It’s only due today, and you’ve come up to ask…We’re moving tomorrow, moving…”

The landlady laughed awkwardly, said a few polite words, and left.

His wife was clearing the table to eat dinner and asked, “Isn’t today the day you get paid?”

He was silent for a moment, picked up the bowl of rice from the table, and said, “It’s already been given out, I didn’t receive it. I’ll go to the accounting office tomorrow…”

His wife didn’t ask him further. But he put the chopsticks down hard on the table, and said angrily, “This unlucky thing! I can only get fifteen big ones.”

“Why?”

“Lost it, miscalculated the accounts when checking the luggage tickets.”

His wife almost jumped up, and said with a sullen face: “Oh my, working for a month like crazy, and still losing money on such a small matter, what’s the point?”

How will we live this month? He thought silently, and gradually, gradually, his vision filled with scattered, intangible black shadows again.

To Mr. Wu Jiayan: Seeing the newspaper report that a child is unable to attend school due to a poor family background, someone is willing to sponsor the child's education to fulfill their desire to learn. If there are parents or guardians, please contact Mr. Zhou Xinwei at our editorial department (every day from 7 PM to 9 PM) for an introduction.

New Song Introduction

Sickle Dance Song, Lyrics by Tao Zhixing

The sun rises over the mountains, Yahe Hai, the sickle is shining, Hhehe, encountering grass, cutting Mei Qizi Suo, bundling it up to burn, seeing grandma Hhehe.

The sun is overhead, Yahe Shi, chop chop a Hhehe, sister-in-law, listen a Mei Qizi Suo, good flowers cut chop, no wearing Hhehe.

The sun is setting, Yahe Hai, chop chop a Hhehe, sister-in-law, look a Mei Qizi Suo, if the seedlings are not kept, the autumn mountain is bald Hhehe.

The sun goes down, Yahe Hai, cut clean Hhehe, the spring wind blows and grows again Mei Qizi Suo, leaving many seeds, knife knife Hhehe.

Temptation—Wireless Radio Drama Script by Theater Performers (24) 201

— Written by Liu Yawei

Relief Worker: Follow me out!

Another Worker: Those who are not named are not allowed to pass as fish eyes mixed with pearls. If it is found out, no big cake will be given tonight!

One Disaster Victim: Mother of my child, let's just count it as tomorrow! (The people leaving are rushing towards the dock, and the groans of those who remain are gradually disappearing! The north wind is particularly strong at this dusk. Although it is not a severe winter, those who are blown here are severely lacking in nutrition. Of course, among the individual sounds, there is an intellectual pronouncement!)

Ship Manager: Those who got the big cake, get on the ship, line up well, don't push, you won't be saved if you fall into the river!

(People are boarding one after another! The discordant human voices are noisy, among which there must be quite a bit of excitement!)

A Disaster Woman: Sir: Our old mother is very sick. Do you see if there is any way to help her?

Relief Worker: Then you don't have to leave today, go back and ask them to think of a way to help her!

A Disaster Woman: (Responding) Okay! (Sobbing, she supports a moaning old mother and goes back!)

Narrative Ballad 202

Cai Xiaofang's Record of Retribution

Zhongxi (1040) 1:00 PM to 1:45 PM

Opening, "Woman Crying Over Agarwood," the autumn scene, osmanthus is fragrant in August. A passionate woman cries in her boudoir. Only hearing, the cold insects chirping outside the window. The wind blows the purple bamboo rustling. The iron horse under the eaves rings. Secretly lowers her head, thinking to herself. Thinking of the handsome and talented man from her mother's home. She married into her husband's family for less than half a month. The maid sent a letter to her room. Saying the talented man is ill in bed. She is like a incense altar, making an empty bow. Praying to the heavens and the city god. Wishing him peace and health. She married into her husband's family for less than a month. The maid sent a letter to her room. Saying the talented man's life is fleeting. Making her, cry to death several times before she is resurrected. Her husband asks her why she is sad. She only says her stomach aches, it is hard to bear. She should have offered condolences before his spirit. Only because she is a new bride less than a month married. Not attending the funeral in the hall. She can only secretly wear three points of mourning. Tying a piece of linen cloth to her chest. Not wearing red or green clothes. Only wearing two plain pieces of clothing. A pair of embroidered shoes with linen on them. Asking the maid to buy a piece of agarwood. She carves the talented man's handsome face. Carving him wearing a square scarf with double ribbons. White jade in the center shining. Wearing a dark blue gown with a light yellow belt. Red satin shoes with black satin trim. She has trouble carving you, pacing back and forth in the study. Difficult to carve you. Opening your mouth to call her younger sister. Difficult to carve you. Playing chess across from each other, watching "The West Chamber." Difficult to carve you. Urging several times, difficult to separate. Only because the bridal sedan chair arrives at the hall. She has to grit her teeth and say goodbye to the talented man. When turning around, she cries sadly. The idle people only talk idle talk. Only saying she is reluctant to leave her parents. How would they know. She is reluctant to part with a affectionate and righteous talented man. Talented man, she says you open your mouth for offerings on the dressing table. In the evening. Using the green gauze curtain as a shrine. There are so many sad things in the world. Others' sadness can be mourned. Her sadness is hidden in her stomach.

Movies

Saturday · Jincheng · Spring Flower · 205

Wu Cun's "Spring Flower" has been decided for its screening period, starting this Saturday at the Jincheng Theater.

"Spring Flower" is an extremely beautiful and lighthearted story, full of "knowing smiles" of satire, full of side-splitting gags, and with two sweet love songs, "Spring Flower" and "Wildflower Fragrance," slowly arrive in Shanghai's human world.

Wu Cun himself introduces this movie: "Spring Flower" is like a piece of music without a title, a painting without commentary. You can get the amount it is prepared to give according to how much sympathy you have. It is best if you laugh at it, laugh to anger, laugh to disgust. My tears are dripping, waiting for people who are willing to laugh at it like this.

Gao Zhanfei, Yan Yuexian, Huang Naishuang, Zhu Qiuzhuang, Sun Min, Xie Yunqing, and Quan Guangzhao, these people who are very trusted by the public, are the souls of "Spring Flower."

"Spring Flower," Jincheng Theater, starting this Saturday.

The United States recently had a birth of five boys. The Fox Company specially produced the film "Cauntey Doctor," which will be released in China soon.

Silver Snippets 206

— Zhi Er

Charlie Chaplin arrived in Shanghai and lingered in Nanshi, unable to tear himself away. After that, he saw "Burning Red Lotus Temple". According to his Shanghai impressions, he said: "Too excited." What is included in this "too excited"? It's better not to say. Saying it will make some people too "disappointed."

After Charlie Chaplin watched "Burning Red Lotus Temple," the communal stage used it as an advertisement. This can indeed be done, there is no need to discuss it. However, by analogy, our film "Burning Red Lotus Temple" can also be exported, with the advertisement saying: "The 'Burning Red Lotus Temple' that Charlie Chaplin enjoyed watching is now specially transported to be dedicated to Westerners." I wonder if our Grand Premier Zhang also has this intention?

(Confucius said: The shallow Wang Gong can be advised.)

Anna May Wong was rejected by the Taishan Compatriot Association in the four rural areas, so our "American star" had to leave Hong Kong in disappointment. Shanghai has given her gracious treatment, banquets and revelry, fearing that important people and celebrities would hear about it, I wonder what they would think?

(Confucius said: If you hear that you are invited to take a group photo, I wonder what you would think?)

According to Wu Han's news, the editor of "Twentieth Century" is going to be replaced. I hope this is a rumor. Otherwise, … Heavens!

(Confucius said: The history of March's season, the melancholic rain, the sighs of the six-stringed lute!)

In addition to "certain people often using pseudonyms to promote themselves and deceive the masses," there is a more wonderful method: asking friends to write (maybe using a pseudonym themselves) manuscripts such as "talent is not declining," and then asking celebrities to forward them to the other party's newspaper. In this way, "praise surges," and "talent" naturally "commercializes."
